Brown v. State


No. W2010-01131-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 709


May 3, 2011, Assigned on Briefs 
September 9, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court is Affirmed and Remanded. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 01-08323-34. John P. Colton, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court is Affirmed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: The inmate's argument on appeal from the denial of his petition for postconviction relief was that he received an illegal sentence because both boxes were checked on his judgment forms for especially aggravated kidnapping indicating that his sentences should run at 30 and 100 percent. However, the appellate court agreed with the postconviction court that the error was clerical and that his plea was voluntarily and knowingly entered. A remand was solely for entry of corrected forms to reflect a single release eligibility of 100 percent for the his especially aggravated kidnapping convictions.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed and remanded.

State v. Patterson


No. M2010-02360-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 657


June 21, 2011, Session 
August 22, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Williamson County. No. 1-CR094413. Jeffrey S. Bivins, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged an order denying his motion to suppress evidence, arguing that the officer stopped him without reasonable suspicion or probable cause to believe he was driving while impaired in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-10-401. The evidence did not preponderate against the trial court's determination that the officer had reasonable suspicion to stop defendant. The officer testified that defendant was swerving and crossing over the lines marking the lanes, and there was a lack of definitive proof about defendant's driving from the video recording of the traffic stop.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Reid v. State

DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Circuit Court for Montgomery County and the Criminal Court for Davidson County are Affirmed.

OVERVIEW: The State was entitled to conduct a mental health evaluation of defendant under Tenn. Furthermore, during a status hearing the State mentioned that it might rely on the expertise of the evaluators. Counsel voiced no objection about the State's announcement.


OUTCOME: The judgments were affirmed.

Bane v. State

State v. Word


No. M2011-00082-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 556


May 17, 2011, Session 
July 18, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Reversed and Dismissed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Putnam County. No. 10-0762. Leon Burns, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Reversed and Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Petitioner juvenile appealed a judgment that denied his petition for postconviction relief. The appellate court found, inter alia, that the warrant and the citation supporting it alleged that a juvenile violated different code sections. Neither instrument recited the facts underlying the offense of underage drinking. Consequently, because the charging instrument did not comply with Tenn. Const. art. I, § 9, the trial court lacked jurisdiction to entertain the juvenile's plea and the prosecution was invalid.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed, conviction vacated, and charges dismissed.

State v. Patlan


No. M2011-01175-CCA-RM-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 558



July 18, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at Patlan-Cano v. State, 2013 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 630 (Tenn. Crim. App., July 25, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 2006-D-3184. Steve R. Dozier, Judge. Remanded by the Supreme Court May 26, 2011.
State v. Patlan, 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 529 (Tenn., May 26, 2011)



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Evidence was sufficient to sustain defendant's conviction for first degree felony murder during the perpetration of aggravated child abuse under a party theory pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-11-401 because defendant and co-defendant shared physical custody of the victim until his death, and the victim was under eight years old and suffered serious bodily injury. The medical examiner's autopsy showed that the victim suffered second and third degree burns within two weeks of his death as the result of being immersed in scalding hot water, and the burns could not have been accidental.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Medley


No. M2009-02446-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 527


October 26, 2010, Assigned on Briefs 
July 12, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Medley, 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 1076 (Tenn., Nov. 16, 2011)
Post-conviction relief denied at Medley v. State, 2012 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 539 (Tenn. Crim. App., July 16, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part; Vacated in Part; and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Bedford County. No. 16402. Robert Crigler, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part; Vacated in Part; and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of five counts of rape of a child, violations of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-522, and was sentenced consecutively to 25 years for one count and 15 years for each of the other counts. The evidence was sufficient where the victim was 12 years old and described each act of sexual contact with defendant in sufficient detail to establish that penetration occurred. However, the trial court was statutorily required to impose 25-year sentences for each of the five convictions pursuant to § 39-13-522(b)(2)(A). Furthermore, § 39-13-522(b)(2)(A) was found to be constitutional.


OUTCOME: Judgments affirmed in part, vacated in part, and remanded.

Keen v. State


No. W2011-00789-CCA-R28-PD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 972



June 29, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Keen v. State, 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 1195 (Tenn., Dec. 14, 2011)
Affirmed by Keen v. State, 398 S.W.3d 594, 2012 Tenn. LEXIS 932 (Tenn., Dec. 20, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. P25157.
State v. Keen, 31 S.W.3d 196, 2000 Tenn. LEXIS 565 (Tenn., Oct. 5, 2000)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Because petitioner's claim of actual innocence only applied to his sentence of death and not to the offenses for which he was convicted, he could not rely upon Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-117(a)(2) to reopen post-conviction proceedings; [2]-The Tennessee Supreme Court's decision in Coleman v. State did not create a new constitutional rule of law, but involved statutory construction based upon existing law that the parties and trial court had been practicing; [3]-Accordingly, petitioner was not entitled to reopen post-conviction proceedings pursuant to § 40-30-117(a)(1).


OUTCOME: The application for permission to appeal was denied.

State v. Echols


No. E2009-01697-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 442


September 28, 2010, Session 
June 14, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by State v. Echols, 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 989 (Tenn., Oct. 21, 2011)
Affirmed by State v. Echols, 2012 Tenn. LEXIS 738 (Tenn., Oct. 10, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court is Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Knox County. No. 82476. Bob R. McGee, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court is Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction for first-degree felony murder committed during the perpetration of robbery under Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 39-13-202(a)(2) and 39-13-401(a) was proper because the jury could have concluded beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant demanded money from the victim, shot the victim three times, was then shot at by the mortally-wounded victim, and took the victim's wallet. The evidence was sufficient to show that defendant did not shoot the victim in self-defense and that he was guilty of the crime.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Howell v. State


No. W2009-02426-CCA-R3-PD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 447


December 7, 2010, Session 
June 14, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Howell v. State, 2013 Tenn. LEXIS 22 (Tenn., Jan. 9, 2013)
US Supreme Court certiorari dismissed by Howell v. Tennessee, 2014 U.S. LEXIS 8 (U.S., Jan. 7, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court is Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. P-14334. W. Otis Higgs, Jr., Judge.
Howell v. State, 151 S.W.3d 450, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 958 (Tenn., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court is Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: The postconviction court did not err in denying relief based on the inmate's claimed intellectual disability pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-203, because the inmate failed to establish, by a preponderance of the evidence, that he had a significantly subaverage general intellectual functioning as evidenced by an IQ of 70 or below, or that he had deficits in adaptive behavior, such as his day to day functioning. Since the inmate did not demonstrate a subaverage general intellectual functioning or deficit in adaptive behavior, he could not show a manifestation prior to the age of 18.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Pruitt


No. W2009-01255-CCA-R3-DD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 431


July 13, 2010, Session 
June 13, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by State v. Pruitt, 2013 Tenn. LEXIS 778 (Tenn., Oct. 8, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 06-00460. Chris B. Craft, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: In a felony murder case, imposition of the death penalty was upheld where defendant provided no substantial evidence of deficits in adaptive behavior to support a finding of intellectual disability. The trial court did not err in rejecting the scores from defendant's intelligence quotient (I.Q.) tests, where the experts opined defendant did not put forth his best effort. Evidence that defendant ambushed the elderly victim, inflicting numerous blows, and drove away in an attempt to steal the victim's car for parts supported the aggravating factor in Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-204(i)(7).


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

417 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Reagan v. State


No. M2009-02291-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 368


July 21, 2010, Assigned on Briefs 
May 23, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court is Reversed and Dismissed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Overton County. No. 4594. David A. Patterson, Judge.
Reagan v. State, 2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 70 (Tenn. Crim. App., Feb. 2, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court is Reversed and Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On remand, the Circuit Court for Overton County, Tennessee, found petitioner's request for post-conviction relief was untimely under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-102. However, it concluded that due process required the tolling of the limitations period as his trial counsel failed to withdraw under Tenn. Sup. Ct. R. 14. It reviewed the merits of the petition and concluded that petitioner was not entitled to post-conviction relief. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: On petitioner's appeal from the denial of his original petition, the court questioned the timeliness of the petition and remanded for a determination of whether it was in accordance with § 40-30-102 or whether due process required tolling of the limitations period. The circuit court found that trial counsel's failure to file a motion to withdraw was a misrepresentation to petitioner of his intention to pursue an application for permission to appeal to the supreme court, which denied petitioner the right to seek post-conviction relief. Thus, the statute of limitations was tolled. While the court agreed that trial counsel made serious missteps in his representation of petitioner, it concluded that due process did not require the tolling of the limitations period. By his own admission, petitioner called trial counsel and knew he was on his own a couple of months after his convictions had been affirmed on direct appeal. At that point, he had nearly 10 months to timely file his petition. Thus, the circuit court improperly determined that the statute of limitations should be tolled.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court and dismissed the post-conviction relief petition.

Wallace v. Dotson


No. W2010-01784-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 360


January 5, 2011, Assigned on Briefs 
May 17, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hardeman County. No. 10-CR-114. Joseph H. Walker, III, Judge.
Wallace v. State, 2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 97 (Tenn. Crim. App., Feb. 6, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: The judgment summarily dismissing petitioner inmate's petition for a writ of habeas corpus was appropriate. Although the inmate argued that he was entitled to habeas corpus relief because he was innocent of the charges, claims for the sufficiency of the evidence were not cognizable in a habeas corpus proceeding. The inmate was charged and held liable for the victim's death as a principal. However, even if he was not charged with or found guilty of the death as a principal, an instruction on the natural and probable consequences rule was not required.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

419 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Suttles v. State


No. E2008-02146-CCA-R3-PD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 305


June 29, 2010, Session 
April 29, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Suttles v. State, 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 1113 (Tenn., Nov. 16, 2011)
Request denied by Suttles v. State, 2017 Tenn. LEXIS 296 (Tenn., May 28, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Criminal Court for Knox County. No. 72245. Mary Beth Leibowitz, Judge.
State v. Suttles, 30 S.W.3d 252, 2000 Tenn. LEXIS 360 (Tenn., June 26, 2000)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Criminal Court for Knox County (Tennessee), which denied his motion for post-conviction relief after he was convicted of premeditated first-degree murder and sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that trial counsel failed to select appropriate experts, failed to supervise properly the experts they retained, and failed to provide the experts with the information necessary to evaluate defendant. The court upheld the decision. The court agreed with the post-conviction court's conclusion that trial counsel made a reasonably informed strategic decision to employ the services of a psychiatric evaluation expert. The expert never voiced concern to the trial attorneys about any conflict of interest regarding his involvement in first degree murder trial. Trial counsel weighed the negative impact that the expert's prior prison evaluations may have had on the jury. However, because the expert was intimately more familiar with defendant and because his opinion about the defendant's mental state at the time of the murder was extremely favorable to the defense theory of the case, trial counsel decided the positive aspects of the expert's testimony outweighed any negative implications regarding defendant's previous incarceration. Just because trial counsel's judgment might have been wrong was not sufficient to prove incompetent representation had occurred.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

420 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Allen v. State


No. M2009-02151-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 287


August 18, 2010, Session 
April 26, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Allen v. State, 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 819 (Tenn., Aug. 25, 2011)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Allen v. Tennessee, 132 S. Ct. 1639, 182 L. Ed. 2d 238, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 1705 (U.S., 2012)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Partial summary judgment granted by Allen v. Colson, 953 F. Supp. 2d 870, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 87047 (M.D. Tenn., 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. A-1004. Monte Watkins, Judge.
Allen v. White, 185 Fed. Appx. 487, 2006 U.S. App. LEXIS 16322 (6th Cir.) (6th Cir. Tenn., 2006)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: In petitioner's first-degree murder case, the court's instructions on reasonable doubt were not improper because the court provided a context for the jury to understand that, when it referred to "moral certainty," it referred to certainty "with respect to human affairs" and not moral conviction; thus, nothing suggested a higher degree of doubt than that which was necessary for an acquittal under the reasonable doubt standard. As such, although the court employed the term "moral certainty," the instruction correctly conveyed the concept of reasonable doubt to the jury.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Pike v. State


No. E2009-00016-CCA-R3-PD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 285


April 14, 2010, Session 
April 25, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Pike v. State, 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 1110 (Tenn., Nov. 15, 2011)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Pike v. Tenn., 2012 U.S. LEXIS 6877 (U.S., Oct. 1, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Knox County. No. 68280. Mary Beth Leibowitz, Judge.
Pike v. State, 2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 635 (Tenn. Crim. App., July 15, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: Post-conviction court's presiding over petitioner's motion for postconviction relief was proper under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-105 because, although the court was party to an in-camera meeting between the parties, nothing in the record supported petitioner's theory or supposition. The post-conviction court's comment in no way led to a conclusion that it was harboring under a veil of impartiality with regard to the decision. Nor was the court's mere presence at the meeting a sufficient reason to force the court's disqualification.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

422 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Maclin v. State


No. W2010-00123-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 193



March 15, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Maclin v. State, 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 712 (Tenn., July 14, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20 of the Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 96-07198. John P. Colton, Jr., Judge.
State v. Maclin, 1998 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 877 (Tenn. Crim. App., Aug. 21, 1998)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20 of the Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was convicted of second degree murder. After affirmance on direct appeal, petitioner's claim for post-conviction relief was denied and the decision was affirmed on appeal. The Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) denied petitioner's subsequent claim for post-conviction relief. Petitioner appealed and the State filed a motion requesting the court to affirm the post-conviction court's order pursuant to Tenn. Ct. Crim. App. R. 20.


OVERVIEW: The State argued, inter alia, that the Post-Conviction Procedure Act clearly provided that second or successive petitions must be summarily dismissed. The State claimed that because the petitioner's first post-conviction petition was heard and decided on its merits and the petitioner was able to appeal that decision, the new post-conviction petition failed to present any meritorious grounds for relitigating this case. The court of criminal appeals agreed. Pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-102(c), in no event may more than one (1) petition for post-conviction relief be filed attacking a single judgment. Under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-102(c), if a prior petition had been filed, which was resolved on the merits by a court of competent jurisdiction, any second or subsequent petition "shall" be summarily dismissed. Petitioner's first post-conviction petition was resolved on its merits and the lower court acted properly in summarily dismissing her second post-conviction petition on that basis.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed pursuant to Tenn. Ct. Crim. App. R. 20.

Deakins v. State


No. W2010-00020-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 188


November 2, 2010, Assigned on Briefs at Knoxville 
March 11, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Deakins v. State, 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 715 (Tenn., July 15, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Lauderdale County Circuit Court. No. 6360. Joe H. Walker, III, Judge.
State v. Deakins, 2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 25 (Tenn. Crim. App., Jan. 11, 2010)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a summary dismissal by the Lauderdale County Circuit Court (Tennesssee) of his pro se petition for habeas corpus relief from his conviction for especially aggravated sexual exploitation of a minor in violation of the Tennessee Protection of Children Against Sexual Explotation Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-17-1005(a) (Supp. 2000) (amended 2005).


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court erred by finding that the judgment was not void and by dismissing his petition without an evidentiary hearing and without appointment of counsel. Specifically, defendant argued that the State violated constitutional ex post facto prohibitions when it charged him under the Tennessee Protection of Children Against Sexual Exploitation Act (PCSEA), Tenn. Code Ann, § 39-17-1005(a) (Supp. 2000) (amended 2005). The court upheld the decision. Defendant argued that he did not waive constitutional issues by pleading guilty because his plea was not voluntary. He claimed that the trial court failed to explain the consequences of violating probation at the guilty plea proceedings. The court held that voluntariness of the guilty plea was not relevant to a habeas corpus proceeding as a matter of law. Accordingly, defendant's claim regarding the constitutionality of the statute was previously decided on post-conviction appeal and was not appropriate for habeas corpus relief. The court also found that the indictment was sufficient to vest jurisdiction in the trial court even though the statute mentioned in the indictment had changed.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

State v. Graves


No. E2009-00009-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 91


January 26, 2010, Session 
February 8, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Graves, 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 508 (Tenn., May 27, 2011)
Post-conviction relief denied at Graves v. State, 2014 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1008 (Tenn. Crim. App., Nov. 4, 2014)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied, Motion denied by, Dismissed by Graves v. Cook, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 162008 (E.D. Tenn., Sept. 28, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court are Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Knox County. No. 83856. Richard R. Baumgartner, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court are Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal Court for Knox County (Tennessee) of first degree premeditated murder and felony murder committed during the perpetration of a kidnapping. The trial court merged the convictions and sentenced defendant to life in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to show the element of premeditation under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-202. The court of appeals disagreed. The evidence established that defendant thought the victim had burglarized his apartment and had taken eight hundred dollars and some tools. By defendant's own admission, he was "mad." Defendant allegedly believed the victim was dangerous. However, instead of contacting the police, defendant got a gun and went to the motel to confront the victim. He forced his way into the victim's motel room, and beat the victim with the weapon. Defendant did not find any of his property in the victim's room. Although he claimed he only wanted the victim to return his property, he then kidnapped the unarmed victim and continued beating the victim in the car. The medical examiner's testimony established that defendant beat the victim severely, causing skull fractures, hemorrhaging under the scalp, and brain contusions. When the victim escaped from the car, defendant followed and shot him at least six times. Defendant then drove to a store where he bought cleaning supplies and cleaned the victim's blood off the backseat.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Patlan


No. M2008-02515-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 89


June 22, 2010, Session 
February 4, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by State v. Patlan, 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 529 (Tenn., May 26, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 2006-D-3184. Steve Dozier, Judge.
State v. Dorantes, 2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 965 (Tenn. Crim. App., Nov. 30, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) of aggravated child abuse and first degree felony murder during the perpetration of aggravated child abuse. The court denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain her convictions. The court of appeals disagreed. It was undisputed that the victim was under eight years old and suffered serious bodily injury. During the time of his abuse and up to his death, the victim was in the exclusive care of defendant and the co-defendant. The victim was visibly injured and in need of medical attention. The co-defendant and defendant knew that the victim needed medical attention, yet neither of them sought medical treatment for the victim. When asked why he did not take the child to the doctor, the co-defendant stated, "since he was not the victim's father he did not have any reason to want to make the victim get better." Whenever someone expressed concern about the victim's condition, defendant provided excuses, which the medical testimony refuted, and fled with the co-defendant. There was no evidence that the co-defendant coerced the defendant or that defendant attempted to report the abuse or otherwise prevent the victim from being further abused. Moreover, after the victim's death, defendant fled to Mexico.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Jackson v. State


No. M2010-00446-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 83


September 21, 2010, On Brief 
February 1, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court is Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 2001-D-2175. Seth Norman, Judge.
State v. Jackson, 2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 339 (Tenn. Crim. App., Apr. 12, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court is Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of the dismissal of his second petition for writ of habeas corpus by the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee). Petitioner argued that his sentence, requiring a 100 percent release eligibility, was unconstitutional and was contrary to the Tennessee Criminal Sentencing Reform Act of 1989. The habeas corpus court summarily dismissed the petition based upon the fact that petitioner had previously raised the issue.


OVERVIEW: The trial court sentenced petitioner to thirty-six years to be served at 100 percent for his conviction of possession with intent to sell. On review, the court noted that the formal requirements for a petition for a writ of habeas corpus were set forth in Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-21-107. The court stated that the issues raised by petitioner had been previously adjudicated on the appeal from his first petition for writ of habeas corpus. On appeal of the denial of that petition, the court had determined that petitioner was mistaken that he was not required to serve 100 percent of the minimum sentence for the applicable range. Nothing on the face of the judgment in the record indicated that the trial court was without authority to impose an enhanced sentence pursuant to the Drug-Free School Zone statute, Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-17-432(c). The court concluded that its previous adjudication of the issues in question barred petitioner from raising the same issues again in his second habeas corpus petition.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the petition.

January 28, 2011, Filed

Related proceeding at Sims v. Colson, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 56158 (W.D. Tenn., Mar. 23, 2012)
Post-conviction proceeding at Sims v. State, 2014 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1179 (Tenn. Crim. App., Feb. 5, 2014)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Request denied by Sims v. State, 2016 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 613 (Tenn. Crim. App., Jan. 28, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. P-25898. Chris Craft, Judge.
State v. Sims, 45 S.W.3d 1, 2001 Tenn. LEXIS 349 (Tenn., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, sentenced to death for first degree murder, challenged an order of the Shelby County Criminal Court (Tennessee) denying his initial and amended petitions for post-conviction relief pursuant to the Post-Conviction Procedure Act of 1995.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner argued on appeal that the post-conviction court erred in denying his claims that defense counsel provided ineffective assistance, in violation of the Sixth Amendment. The appeals court disagreed that red flags listed by petitioner necessarily triggered the need for a neuropsychological evaluation, and did not find that trial counsel was deficient for not requesting one. Trial counsel testified that neither petitioner, his family, nor anyone else ever indicated that petitioner had any type of emotional or psychological problems or mental illness, disease, or defect. Even if trial counsel was deficient in failing to order a neuropsychological evaluation, petitioner failed to show that he was prejudiced. Petitioner also contended that trial counsel was ineffective for failing to preserve for appellate review the trial court's exclusion of evidence regarding petitioner's lack of remorse. However, the post-conviction court found that because the testimony would have come from petitioner's mother rather than petitioner, the jury would have given it little weight. The appeals court concluded that petitioner failed to demonstrate entitlement to post-conviction relief.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

434 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Harvey


No. E2008-01081-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1095


June 23, 2009, Session 
December 30, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Reversed, Case Remanded. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Knox County. No. 79665. Ray Lee Jenkins, Judge (trial); Kenneth F. Irvine, Judge (motion for new trial).



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Reversed, Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal Court for Knox County (Tennessee) of assault and disorderly conduct. Defendant was sentenced to eleven-months, twenty-nine days on probation for the assault conviction and to thirty days on probation for the disorderly conduct conviction, with the sentences to run concurrently. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in not granting a mistrial after substituting a previously excused alternate for a disqualified juror under Tenn. R. Crim. P. 24. The court of criminal appeals agreed. Defendant did not waive the issue and the procedure violated defendant's constitutional and statutory rights. The trial court substituted a previously discharged juror and instructed the jury to restart its deliberations. That procedure was not only unauthorized by statute or rule, but it was specifically condemned. The trial court expressly and properly discharged the alternate juror after releasing the jury to deliberate. At that point, the discharged alternate was no longer a member of the jury. In short, the procedure the trial court used to later recall the alternate was incorrect. However, especially given the court's instruction to bring the alternate "up to speed," the instruction more naturally read as though the alternate was to be briefed on what had transpired in the deliberations rather than as though the deliberations were to start again from scratch. Therefore, the trial court erred in substituting the alternate juror for the disqualified juror.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial.

State v. Jaimes-Garcia


No. M2009-00891-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1078


May 18, 2010, Session 
December 22, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Jaimes-Garcia, 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 533 (Tenn., May 31, 2011)
Post-conviction relief denied at Jaimes-Garcia v. State, 2016 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 779 (Tenn. Crim. App., Oct. 18, 2016)
Appeal denied by Jaimes-Garcia v. State, 2017 Tenn. LEXIS 122 (Tenn., Feb. 15, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed in part, Reversed in Part and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 2006-D-3175. Mark J. Fishburn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed in part, Reversed in Part and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), which convicted him of multiple drug offenses relating to three different drug sales. An effective sentence of 18 years in the Tennessee Department of Correction was imposed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his various drug convictions and the appellate court concluded that two of the convictions violated his double jeopardy protections. The remainder of the judgment was affirmed. The evidence proved that defendant and another male conspired to sell more than 300 grams of cocaine. The confidential informant contacted the male on several occasions to ask to purchase drugs and both the male and defendant testified that the male then relayed to defendant the details of his conversations with the confidential informant, including the quantity of drugs the informant wished to purchase and the location of the agreed meeting place. Defendant's conviction in Count 7 for the possession of cocaine was improper because he was simultaneously in possession of the cocaine in his home, that was left there when he divided the cocaine to sell the correct amount to the State's confidential informant, and the cocaine that he possessed at the time of that sale. He was convicted for the sale of cocaine, and one must necessarily "possess" cocaine in order to sell that same cocaine. Thus, there was a double jeopardy violation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed in Count 5, convicting defendant of selling more than 300 grams of cocaine, and was to be merged into Count 4; the conviction in Count 7 for possession with intent to sell 0.5 grams or more of cocaine was reversed and dismissed with prejudice; the remainder of the judgment was affirmed.

State v. Reynolds


No. M2009-00185-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1076


May 18, 2010, Session 
December 16, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Reynolds, 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 554 (Tenn., May 25, 2011)
US Supreme Court certiorari dismissed by Reynolds v. Tennessee, 133 S. Ct. 21, 180 L. Ed. 2d 940, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 5212 (U.S., 2011)
Post-conviction relief denied at Reynolds v. State, 2013 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 363 (Tenn. Crim. App., May 1, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Rutherford County. No. F-61326. Don R. Ash, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Rutherford County (Tennessee), which convicted him of first-degree premeditated murder in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-202(a)(1) (2001) and sentenced him to life in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for first-degree premeditated murder and his sentence of life in prison, but the appellate court affirmed, stating that the evidence was sufficient for the jury to have found that defendant acted with premeditation. Defendant was calm shortly after the killing and he returned to a friend's house, got in bed, and told her that he had killed the victim, with whom he had a child. Defendant then went to sleep, woke up, and engaged in normal daily activities. The victim was also unarmed and shot repeatedly in the back of her head. Defendant had a motive for killing the victim in that the two were involved in a highly contested custody dispute and defendant admittedly "hated" the victim. Further, the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it determined that the evidence that a female communicated with the victim via a hoax MySpace page and was in Tennessee on the weekend of the victim's murder was not relevant. The female explained the reason she created the MySpace page, and her communications with the victim were benign.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

438 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sexton


No. E2008-00292-CCA-R3-DD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1035


August 25, 2009, Session 
December 7, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by State v. Sexton, 2012 Tenn. LEXIS 377 (Tenn., May 29, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Scott County. No. 7685. E. Shayne Sexton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments Of The Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Criminal Court for Scott County (Tennessee), which convicted him of two counts of first-degree murder in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 39-13-201 and 39-13-202(a) (Supp. 2000) and imposed death sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his first-degree murder convictions and death sentences, but the appellate court affirmed. The record did not support a conclusion that the jurors impaneled were incompetent. Witness testimony delineating defendant's prior bad acts was relevant to establishing a motive for the murders. Considering, however, the numerous admonitions of the trial court to abstain from graphic testimony regarding the nature of the alleged act, the trial court clearly intended to specifically limit that witness's testimony regarding the details of the alleged incident. However, while the information was prejudicial, the danger of unfair prejudice did not outweigh the probative value of the testimony. The proof at trial showed that defendant had a motive for the killing because he blamed one of the victims for the accusation of child sexual abuse. Defendant had threatened to kill that victim prior to the murder, procured a gun substantially similar to the murder weapon just before the murder, and defendant confessed to killing the victims to several witnesses. That was sufficient to show premeditation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Alderson v. State


No. M2010-00896-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1016


October 19, 2010, Assigned on Briefs 
November 30, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at Alderson v. State, 2013 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1052 (Tenn. Crim. App., Dec. 3, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Reversed; Remanded. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 2007-A-708. Seth Norman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Reversed; Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: When she was 16 years old, petitioner plead guilty to two counts of felony murder and one count of attempted first degree murder. She filed a petition for post-conviction relief, which was summarily dismissed by the Criminal Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, because her petition was barred by the statute of limitations. Petitioner sought review.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner argued that the statute of limitations was tolled due to her minority status. The post-conviction court found that her minority status alone was not sufficient to toll the statute of limitations under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-102(a). The court found that the precise issue was whether petitioner was misled by prison officials to believe that her minority status prevented her from filing a petition or tolled the limitations period, which, if true, would entitle her to equitable tolling of the filing period. The court found that petitioner delivered her petition to prison officials within one year from the date she reached majority age and that she appeared to be grossly uneducated. The court concluded that the post-conviction relief court erred in dismissing her petition without conducting a hearing to determine whether due process considerations tolled the statute of limitations based on the alleged actions of the prison officials.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for an evidentiary hearing to determine whether due process tolled the statute of limitations so as to give petitioner a reasonable opportunity after the expiration of the limitations period to present her claim in a meaningful time and manner, and if so, whether petitioner's filing of her post-conviction petition was within the reasonable opportunity afforded by the due process tolling.

Wilson v. State


No. W2008-02439-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 825


September 1, 2009, Session 
September 30, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Reversed and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. P-27290. James C. Beasley, Jr., Judge.
Wilson v. State, 2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1042 (Tenn. Crim. App., Sept. 21, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of the decision of the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee), which denied in part his petition for postconviction relief and ordered a delayed appeal. It determined that appellate counsel was ineffective and that trial counsel were effective.


OVERVIEW: The inmate appealed from the denial in part of his petition for postconviction relief and simultaneous order of a delayed appeal. The postconviction court determined that appellate counsel was ineffective and granted a delayed appeal. It was further determined that trial counsel were effective. The inmate argued on appeal that the postconviction court erred by not setting aside his conviction for felony murder and granting a new trial. The appellate court reversed the postconviction court's determination that trial counsel provided effective assistance of counsel, vacated the inmate's conviction, and remanded for a new trial. The inmate was deprived the effective assistance of counsel at trial. Trial counsel was deficient in failing to request an instruction on second-degree murder and in failing to preserve the issue for appeal. Even though the evidence was clearly sufficient to support a verdict of felony murder, the inmate's conduct also showed that he was criminally responsible for second-degree murder. The error was not harmless because the jury was deprived of the option of considering whether the offense applied, which impaired their truth-ascertainment function.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the determination that trial counsel provided effective assistance of counsel, vacated the petitioner's conviction, and remanded for a new trial. In regard to the inmate's delayed appeal, the appellate court's decision pertaining to trial counsel's performance rendered it moot.

State v. Cooper


No. W2008-01339-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 853


July 14, 2009, Session 
September 29, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Cooper, 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 257 (Tenn., Mar. 9, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court are Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 06-03933. James C. Beasley, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court are Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant pled guilty to one count of possession of more than 300 grams of cocaine with the intent to sell and one count of possession of more than 300 grams of cocaine with the intent to deliver, but reserved a certified question as to the denial of his motion to suppress evidence. The Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) imposed a total effective sentence of 18 years in prison. The defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The defendant's convictions stemmed from the discovery of approximately 85 pounds of cocaine in his vehicle during a traffic stop for failing to slow down or move over while an officer's car was on the side of the road. Prior to trial, the defendant filed a motion to suppress the evidence on the basis that he was placed in the patrol car for a minor traffic violation and that, the subsequent search of his car was unconstitutional. The arresting officer acknowledged that the defendant appeared to have appropriate papers and that he had no reason to believe another crime was being committed until he became suspicious of possible criminal activity because of the defendant's defensive stance, nervousness, and fidgeting. The drugs were discovered initially by a dog sniff during a time reasonably required for the officer to complete the traffic stop. The dog's alerts gave the officer probable cause to search the defendant's car. Dog sniffs are not searches. There was no basis on which to suppress the drugs discovered during the search.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Finnie v. State


No. W2009-00990-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 771


May 4, 2010, Assigned on Briefs 
September 15, 2010, Filed


NOTICE: ORDERED NOT FOR CITATION. PLEASE CONSULT THE TENNESSEE SUPREME COURT RULES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Ordered Not for Citation March 9, 2011.
Appeal denied by Finnie v. State, 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 247 (Tenn., Mar. 9, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Reversed in Part and Remanded. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 00-10540-56. W. Mark Ward, Judge.
State v. Finnie, 2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 694 (Tenn. Crim. App., July 8, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Reversed in Part and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed from the post-conviction judgment of the Criminal Court for Shelby County granting him partial post-conviction relief in the form of a delayed appeal from multiple aggravated rape, aggravated robbery, and facilitation of aggravated rape convictions that followed a spree of incidents participated in by the inmate and an accomplice.


OVERVIEW: On appeal of the post-conviction trial court's findings of ineffective assistance of the inmate's trial and appellate counsel, the court held that the offenses were signature offenses and properly consolidated by the original trial court. The inmate and his accomplice used the same methods to commit the offenses, including posing as customers of adult entertainment and preaching to victims after raping them. Counsel also was not shown to be ineffective regarding consecutive sentencing because references of the sentencing judge to the horrible nature of the crimes and the fairness of the aggregate 128-year term for the inmate contained sufficient, if less than precise, findings. However, appellate counsel provided ineffective assistance by not raising the State's failure to elect offenses. The inmate was entitled to unanimous verdicts and when the State presented evidence showing more than one offense occurred, it was the responsibility of the trial court to require the State to elect which offense was being submitted to the jury. Also, to avoid convicting the inmate for acts of the accomplice, the State had to elect which acts were being relied on for the conviction of the inmate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the post-conviction court in part, vacated the inmate's convictions relating to four of the indictments against him, and remanded for new trials on those indictments.

State v. Smith


No. M2009-01144-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 714


July 20, 2010, Session 
August 31, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Smith, 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 55 (Tenn., Jan. 13, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Sumner County. No. 330-1998. C.L. Rogers, Judge.
State v. Smith, 1998 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 24 (Tenn. Crim. App., Jan. 7, 1998)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Criminal Court for Sumner County (Tennessee), which, on the ground of the one-year statute of limitations, dismissed defendant's petition for a writ of error coram nobis, which alleged the existence of newly discovered evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to life imprisonment. He filed a petition for a writ of error coram nobis, in which he alleged the existence of newly discovered evidence. The trial court dismissed the petition based upon the statute of limitations of Tenn. Code Ann. § 27-7-103. On appeal, defendant contended the dismissal was an unconstitutional denial of his right to due process. The trial court was not required to hold an evidentiary hearing because the petition failed to meet the necessary prerequisites to file for such relief. The limitations period had expired almost eleven years before defendant filed his petition. In determining whether the grounds for relief arose after the limitations period normally would have commenced, the appellate court examined the narrative defendant relied upon in his petition. The narrative contained a dialogue between a police officer and defendant, which was necessarily known to defendant at the time it occurred as he was a participant in the dialogue. Therefore, defendant's ground for relief was not "later-arising" and did not require the tolling of the statute of limitations.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment.

OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed and the action was remanded to the trial court.

451 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Banks


No. M2008-01823-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 644


October 20, 2009, Session 
July 26, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Banks, 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 1209 (Tenn., Dec. 14, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Coffee County. No. 35,186. Charles Lee, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Coffee County (Tennessee) found defendant guilty of attempt to initiate of a process intended to result in the manufacture of methamphetamine in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-17-435, and possession of drug paraphernalia. Defendant appealed asserting that the trial court erred in denying his motion to dismiss the indictment as the language in § 39-17-435 was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that an ordinary person would not know what conduct was prohibited because § 39-17-435 did not define the terms, "any substance," "active modification," or "extraction." The court held, however, that those terms were commonly used words capable of being understood by a person of ordinary intelligence, and, although broad in a general sense, § 39-17-435 required that they had to be done knowingly to result in the manufacture of methamphetamine. Further, § 39-17-435 clearly stated that a person should not engage in one of the three delineated acts with knowledge that the acts would lead to the production of methamphetamine. Therefore, because the steps which comprised the initiation offense had to be undertaken "knowingly," a person who inadvertently heated or mixed substances which were commonly used in the manufacture of methamphetamine would not be guilty of a crime under the terms of § 39-17-435 unless the State proved that the conduct was undertaken with the intent to initiate a process that would lead to the production of methamphetamine. Accordingly, § 39-17-435 clearly defined the prohibited conduct and was not susceptible to differing interpretations.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

The denial of her petition for writ of error coram nobis was proper because she failed to present her claim within one year of her conviction of especially aggravated robbery becoming final and she was not denied a reasonable opportunity to present her claim; due process did not require tolling of the statute of limitations.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Vacated by, Remanded by Keough v. State, 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 1140 (Tenn., Dec. 9, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. P-24323. Carolyn Blackett, Judge.
State v. Keough, 18 S.W.3d 175, 2000 Tenn. LEXIS 171 (Tenn., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of the decision of the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee), which denied his petition for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The inmate had been convicted of premeditated murder and attempted first-degree murder and was sentenced to death; he currently appealed the denial of his petition for postconviction relief. The appellate court affirmed however, stating that it was unable to conclude that the trial court erred by refusing to grant the inmate a limited right of cross-examination in a capital postconviction proceeding. The inmate was able to claim the privilege or elect to testify; he made a knowing decision to assert the privilege. He also failed to prove that he received the ineffective assistance of counsel. The inmate failed to establish that had the jury had testimony relating to his "chronic alcoholism," that the jury would not have found him guilty of premeditated murder. Additionally, two jurors were questioned as to their ability to disregard their personal experiences and to follow the law and the inmate offered no evidence to establish that the jury ultimately empaneled was biased or unfair. Thus, he failed to establish any prejudice by counsel's failure to more thoroughly question potential jurors.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Sample v. State


No. W2008-02466-CCA-R3-PD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 487


November 10, 2009, Session 
June 15, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Sample v. State, 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 1059 (Tenn., Nov. 12, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. Nos. P-14252, P-10627, P-06948 & P-07021. Chris Craft, Judge.
State v. McKay, 680 S.W.2d 447, 1984 Tenn. LEXIS 951 (Tenn., Oct. 15, 1984)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of the decision of the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee), which dismissed his petition for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: In 1981 a jury convicted the inmate and a codefendant of two counts of felony murder and imposed upon both men a sentence of death. After the denial of postconviction relief, the inmate appealed. However, the appellate court affirmed. The inmate's claims stemmed from allegations that the State wrongfully suppressed evidence. The inmate contended that the State improperly failed to disclose a supplementary offense report, but while that information was favorable to the inmate to some extent, it did not create a reasonable probability that the result of the proceeding would have been different had the evidence been disclosed; thus, there was no Brady violation. Additionally, an anonymous tip was not material and an eyewitness's statement was not exculpatory. The eyewitness's statement did not contradict the multiple witnesses who identified the inmate as one of the robbers; rather it inculpated three other men in the robbery. In regard to his death sentence, the appellate court stated that Tennessee's capital sentencing scheme did not require aggravating factors to be pled in the indictment.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Ritchie v. State


No. E2009-02543-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 474


April 28, 2010, Assigned on Briefs 
June 14, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Ritchie v. State, 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 891 (Tenn., Sept. 22, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Hamilton County. No. 273920. Rebecca J. Stern, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of a judgment from the Criminal Court for Hamilton County, Tennessee, summarily dismissing his third petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner alleged that the crimes occurred on property owned by the Tennessee Valley Authority (TVA), which meant a federal court had exclusive jurisdiction to prosecute him. The trial court dismissed the petition because it was bound by the supreme court's decision on his first petition for a writ of habeas corpus, which found he was not entitled to relief because neither the face of the judgment nor the convicting court's record showed that it lacked jurisdiction. To establish the invalidity of his conviction, he would have had to produce proof outside the record, and a writ of habeas corpus could not issue under such circumstances. Petitioner argued that the supreme court's decision violated the court's duty to interpret statutes according to their intent and purpose and amended the habeas corpus statutes. The court found it was without authority to reconsider the issues that were previously decided by the supreme court. While the convicting court's record established that petitioner committed his crimes on TVA property, it did not establish that the United States owned the land or that the convicting court lacked concurrent jurisdiction to punish petitioner.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

459 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Harris


No. M2008-01819-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 497


November 17, 2009, Session 
June 11, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Appeal Dismissed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Coffee County. No. 28,817. Charles Lee, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty to aggravated sexual battery in the Circuit Court for Coffee County (Tennessee) and, pursuant to the plea agreement, he was sentenced as a violent offender to eight years in the Tennessee Department of Correction. Ten years later, the State filed a motion to amend the judgment order to impose lifetime community supervision. The trial court entered the amended order, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty in 1998 and did not reserve any question of law. In 2008, the State filed a Motion to Amend Judgment Order because the original judgment order failed to mandate lifetime community supervision as required by Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-524, which applied to defendant because he was convicted of aggravated sexual battery under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-504. The corrected judgment order was entered on July 16, 2008. Defendant filed a timely notice of appeal on August 13, 2008. The court held that defendant could not appeal from the corrected judgment order under Tenn. R. App. P. 3. The original judgment order constituted an illegal sentence, which could be corrected at any time. Following entry of the corrected judgment order, defendant could have filed a motion to withdraw his guilty plea pursuant to Tenn. R. Crim. P. 32(f)(2), and he could have appealed the denial of the motion under Tenn. R. App. P. 3(b), or he could have challenged the guilty plea through a post-conviction proceeding. By pleading guilty, defendant waived his right to directly appeal his sentence even though his sentence was amended.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed defendant's appeal.

Leach v. State


No. M2008-02386-CCA-R3-PD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 443


February 17, 2010, Session 
June 4, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Leach v. State, 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 981 (Tenn., Oct. 18, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court is Affirmed. Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 99-D-2508. J. Randall Wyatt, Jr.
State v. Leach, 148 S.W.3d 42, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 741 (Tenn., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court is Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate was convicted of two counts of first degree murder, one count of especially aggravated robbery and one count of aggravated rape. He was sentenced to death for each murder conviction. His convictions and sentences were affirmed on direct appeal. He subsequently petitioned for postconviction relief, which was denied by the Criminal Court for Davidson County, Tennessee. He challenged the denial of postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the inmate argued numerous violations of his constitutional rights, including denial of the effective assistance of counsel under U.S. Const. amend. VI. Initially, the inmate contended that trial counsel failed to seek suppression of statements the inmate made to the police over the telephone prior to his arrest. Affirming, the court noted that the physical evidence against the inmate was overwhelming. Given that evidence, in addition to the fact the inmate's trial testimony was similar in nature to the statements at issue, the court concluded the inmate failed to demonstrate prejudice. Defense counsel encouraged the jury during closing argument to find the inmate guilty of second degree murder instead of first degree murder. The court disagreed with the inmate's argument that this concession was a constructive denial of the assistance of counsel which required no proof of prejudice; there was no doubt about the physical evidence in the case. After reviewing each of the inmate's arguments, the court concluded that the inmate failed to establish that he received the ineffective assistance of counsel during either the guilt or penalty phase of his trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the postconviction court.

State v. March


No. M2007-00701-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


494 S.W.3d 52; 2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 442


June 9, 2009, Session 
June 2, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. March, 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 1109 (Tenn., Nov. 17, 2010)
Related proceeding at State v. March, 395 S.W.3d 738, 2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 63 (Tenn. Crim. App., 2011)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion denied by March v. Sexton, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 85845 (M.D. Tenn., June 18, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court, Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 2005-D-2854. Steve Dozier, Judge.
In re Estate of March v. Levine, 1999 Tenn. App. LEXIS 181 (Tenn. Ct. App., Mar. 17, 1999)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court, Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), which entered a judgment for conspiracy to commit first-degree murder. He was sentenced to 24 years in the Tennessee Department of Correction.


OVERVIEW: A jury found defendant guilty of one count of conspiracy to commit first-degree murder and two counts of solicitation to commit first-degree murder. The trial court merged the solicitation counts into the conspiracy count and entered a judgment for conspiracy to commit first-degree murder. The appellate court affirmed, stating that the indictment sufficiently informed defendant of the charges against him so that he could prepare his defense and not be misled or surprised at trial. Further, the variance did not present a danger that defendant might be prosecuted a second time for the same offense. No constitutionally protected right existed to solicit murder, and as such, Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-12-102 could punish actions that included speech made for the sole purpose of procuring activities that were illegal. Accordingly, U.S. Const. amend. I did not protect solicitation to commit first degree murder and the jury's guilty verdict was constitutional. The trial court also properly admitted evidence of defendant's discussions about express kidnappings because those discussions were integral parts of his solicitation of an inmate's assistance.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

462 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Riggs


No. E2009-00820-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 419


February 23, 2010, Assigned on Briefs 
May 26, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Knox County. No. 84997. Mary Beth Leibowitz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Criminal Court for Knox County (Tennessee), which convicted her of theft of property valued at $ 10,000 or more but less than $ 60,000, a Class C felony, in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 39-14-103 and 39-14-105(4) (2006). The trial court imposed a Range I, six-year sentence to be served on probation consecutive to a one-year sentence in another case and set the amount of restitution at $ 28,600.95.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed her theft conviction, but the appellate court affirmed, stating that the evidence showed that defendant made numerous purchases for her personal use with the business's funds. Defendant and the business owner were the only people who knew the administrator's password, and the owner testified that she did not make the entries that she attributed to defendant. The owner presented proof of losses to her business of $ 11,603.22. The owner and her accountant testified that defendant admitted making many of the purchases in question, including purchases with the gift cards. The jury assessed the credibility of the owner and accountant and accredited the State's proof. Her sentence was appropriate because defendant's actions were complex and the accountant's testimony and written summaries of the transactions were essential to the prosecution of the case. Therefore, accounting fees were a reasonable, necessary expense in the case. Further, the attorney fees incurred were a reasonable expense for a victim who had suffered a substantial loss as a result of criminal activity; thus, the trial court did not err in awarding restitution for the attorney fees.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Nagele


No. E2009-01313-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 414



May 24, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by State v. Nagele, 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 1087 (Tenn., Nov. 10, 2010)
Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Nagele, 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 762 (Tenn., Aug. 25, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Knox County. No. 75138. Bob R. McGee, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion pursuant to Tenn. R. Crim. P. 32(f) to withdraw his guilty plea to attempted aggravated sexual battery following a correction of judgment to reflect that he was subject to community supervision for life pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-524 (2006). The Criminal Court for Knox County (Tennessee) denied the motion. Defendant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his plea was not knowing and voluntary because he was given erroneous advice by counsel or, in the alternative, because the trial court had not advised him of a direct consequence of his plea. In contrast to his testimony before the trial court, defendant claimed that his counsel's inability to advise him on the specifics of the community supervision program constituted erroneous advice. The court concluded that defendant was given neither erroneous advice, nor was he given no advice. Defendant was advised by counsel about the possibility of being subject to § 39-13-524 and made an intelligent choice to plead guilty, hoping that it would not be imposed against him. Defendant was not prejudiced by the trial court's failure to tell him he might be subject § 39-13-524 because his counsel did so. Defendant argued that the community supervision for life statute was unconstitutional. However, the issue was not raised in the trial court. Plain error review was not warranted as defendant failed to show that a clear and unequivocal rule of law had been breached or that a substantial right of his was adversely affected.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed a judgment of the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), which dismissed his petition for writ of habeas corpus in which he alleged that he received ineffective assistance of counsel, that he was subject to an illegal search, seizure and arrest, and that he received an unconstitutional enhancement of his sentences.


OVERVIEW: The inmate had entered guilty pleas to numerous offenses and received an effective sentence of twenty-three years. The challenge to his sentence appeared to challenge the enhancement of his sentence, but because he entered a guilty plea, no enhancement factors were used to determine his sentence.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

State v. Goins


No. E2009-00021-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 388


October 27, 2009, Session 
May 17, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. 3; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Sullivan County. No. S49,095. Robert H. Montgomery, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Criminal Court for Sullivan County (Tennessee), which convicted him of facilitation of second-degree murder and especially aggravated robbery in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-403.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions for facilitation of second-degree murder and especially aggravated robbery, but the appellate court affirmed. Despite defendant's claims that a witness's statements would subject her to criminal liability for facilitation of murder and accessory after the fact, her statements did not support criminal liability for either crime; the statements did not indicate that she knowingly furnished substantial assistance in commission of the felony under Tenn. The trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to sequester the jury in light of the trial court's admonitions to the jury to avoid media coverage of the trial and in light of the jurors' reporting that there were no major violations of the trial court's instructions. The imposition of consecutive sentences was appropriate under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-115(b)(2) given defendant's criminal history.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Hill

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Knox County. No. 84920. Richard Baumgartner, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Criminal Court for Knox County (Tennessee), which convicted him of first-degree premeditated murder in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-202 (2003), and abuse of a corpse in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-17-312. He received an effective sentence of life in prison.

Siler v. State


No. E2009-00436-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 299


August 26, 2009, Assigned on Briefs 
April 12, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Reversed and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Knox County. No. 90960. Mary Beth Leibowitz, Judge.
State v. Siler, 2001 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 299 (Tenn. Crim. App., Apr. 17, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner challenged a judgment of the Criminal Court for Knox County (Tennessee), which summarily dismissed his application for post-conviction relief as untimely. He argued that due process considerations tolled the one-year statute of limitations for post-conviction relief, Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-102(a) (2006), and entitled him to a delayed appeal.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner pleaded guilty to attempted especially aggravated robbery. A jury found him guilty of felony murder. His convictions were affirmed on direct appeal. Petitioner contended that his counsel violated his due process rights by failing to appeal his case to the supreme court after his convictions were affirmed on direct appeal, by failing to withdraw as counsel pursuant to Tenn. Sup. Ct. R. 14, and by failing to argue that petitioner was incompetent because of involuntary intoxication and failure to assert the defense of involuntary intoxication at trial. The court of criminal appeals held that the post-conviction court erred in dismissing the petition without conducting a hearing. Petitioner attached a letter from counsel as proof of counsel's intent to file for a Tenn. R. App. P. 11 appeal as well as a letter from the court clerk as proof of counsel's failure to properly withdraw from his case. Before dismissing the petition as untimely, the post-conviction court was required to conduct a hearing to determine if in fact, petitioner was misled to believe that counsel was continuing the appeals process, thereby requiring the tolling of the limitations period.


OUTCOME: The court of criminal appeals reversed the post-conviction court's summary dismissal of the petition for post-conviction relief and remanded the matter for an evidentiary hearing. On remand, the trial court was also instructed to consider petitioner's claims regarding his mental condition against the standard for mental competency.
