Futch v. State


No. W2009-01678-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 305


February 2, 2010, Session 
April 9, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Reversed and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 07-06992. Lee V. Coffee, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner pleaded guilty in the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) to aggravated sexual battery, a Class B felony. The trial court sentenced him to 8 years, at 100 percent. Proceeding pro se, petitioner sought post-conviction relief. The post-conviction court summarily dismissed the petition. The petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: On June 2, 2008, petitioner pleaded guilty to the charge of aggravated sexual battery, and the trial court entered judgment that day. The court held that the statute of limitations for post-conviction relief did not begin to run until July 2, 2008, thirty days later. Thus, petitioner had until July 2, 2009, to file his petition for post-conviction relief. Therefore, contrary to the post-conviction court's holding, the petition was timely filed under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-102(a). Pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-106(d), the petition alleged claims that, if taken as true, would entitle petitioner to relief, including allegations that petitioner took medications that affected his level of awareness of his surroundings, rendering his confession of guilt unreliable. He asserted that he signed a paper he did understand the contents of, believing that the paper was to drop the charges. He also alleged ineffective assistance of counsel because trial counsel did not call several witnesses, failed to preserve questions of law for appeal, and failed to timely file an appeal. Therefore, petitioner was entitled to appointment of counsel and a hearing pursuant to Tenn. Sup. Ct. R. 28, § 6.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's dismissal of the petition and remanded the case to the trial court for appointment of counsel and a hearing.

Stout v. State


No. M2009-01171-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 279


January 13, 2010, Assigned on Briefs 
April 5, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Stout v. State, 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 758 (Tenn., Aug. 26, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 4029. Cheryl Blackburn, Judge.
Stout v. State, 2002 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 110 (Tenn. Crim. App., Feb. 7, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought a writ of habeas corpus in the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), alleging that his conviction for especially aggravated robbery was void and that his sentence was illegal. The habeas corpus court denied the petition, and petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner alleged that the grand jury foreperson was unconstitutionally selected by a circuit court judge. The court held that this was not a cognizable habeas corpus claim because there was no showing that the trial court was without jurisdiction to sentence petitioner or that petitioner's sentence had expired, as required by Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-21-101 (2006). Petitioner contended that his sentence was illegal due to the trial court ordering him to serve his sentence at 100 percent and 35 percent for only one offense. The court held that the trial court's error in checking two boxes on the judgment form was a clerical error to be remedied by entry of corrected judgments pursuant to Tenn. R. Crim. P. 36. The record clearly indicated that the trial court intended for the sentence to be served at 100 percent; petitioner was convicted by a jury, and his status as a violent offender was an operation of statute, Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-501(i)(2)(E). An illegal sentence was a basis for habeas relief only if the illegality of the sentence was egregious to the point of voidness, and the indication of two sentencing ranges on the judgment form did not rise to this level of egregiousness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the habeas corpus court.

 

471 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Fain v. State


No. M2009-01148-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 212


February 16, 2010, Session 
March 9, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Marion County. No. 8020A. Thomas W. Graham, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner mother, who had been convicted pursuant to her guilty plea of misdemeanor assault and misdemeanor child abuse, sought post-conviction relief in the Circuit Court for Marion County (Tennessee), alleging that she received ineffective assistance of counsel due to her trial counsel's failure to challenge the assault statute, Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-301. The circuit court denied the petition, and the mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother was charged based on allegations that she had held her adopted son's tongue with a pair of pliers and submerged his head in ice water. She argued that the attorney who represented her during her guilty plea proceedings was ineffective because he did not advise her to challenge the constitutionality of the assault statute as applied to her. Her trial counsel testified that he did not consider raising any constitutionality of the statute issue because be felt it was a weak argument and that the mother's extreme conduct alleged went beyond normal corporal punishment. He also testified that the mother appeared to understand her options and chose to plead guilty of her own volition. The court held that the constitutionality of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-101 was not before it. The mother did not testify that she would not have pleaded guilty had her trial counsel raised the issue of the constitutionality of § 39-13-301. No other witness offered testimony that her decision to plead guilty was predicated on a lack of discussion of the assault statute's constitutionality.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the post-conviction court.

McKinney v. State


No. W2006-02132-CCA-R3-PD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 219


June 3, 2008, Session 
March 9, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by McKinney v. State, 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 786 (Tenn., Aug. 25, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
T.R.A.P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Reversed; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. P-26860. Arthur T. Bennett, Judge.
State v. McKinney, 74 S.W.3d 291, 2002 Tenn. LEXIS 155 (Tenn., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Reversed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed from the Criminal Court for Shelby County, Tennessee, which denied his petition for postconviction relief. The inmate was previously found guilty of first degree murder and attempted second degree murder. For the capital conviction, the jury sentenced the inmate to death. The inmate presented eight claims, six of which addressed the alleged ineffectiveness of counsel.


OVERVIEW: The evidence presented at the postconviction evidentiary hearing revealed that counsel knew of or should have known of numerous contradicting identifications by witnesses to the shooting. By failing to cross-examine a police officer effectively as to his conflicting statements regarding his identification of the shooter, trial counsel left the jury with essentially unrebutted and untested testimony. Granting a new trial, the court stated that trial counsel's failure to use the prior statements of the officer, as well as the failure to use conflicting identifications of other witnesses, failed to subject the prosecution's case adequately to the adversarial process. Consistent with the court's conclusion that the inmate was prejudiced by counsel's failure to use and present information which would have attacked the credibility of the prosecution's eyewitness testimony and implicated another person at the guilt phase, the court determined that a reasonable probability existed that if counsel had introduced that same evidence as "residual doubt" evidence in the penalty phase, the outcome would have been different.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court denying postconviction relief and granted a new trial.

 

473 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Odom


No. W2008-02464-CCA-R3-DD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 223


November 10, 2009, Session 
March 4, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 91-07049. Chris Craft, Judge.
State v. Odom, 137 S.W.3d 572, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 452 (Tenn., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) of first degree murder committed in the perpetration of rape and was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that his constitutional rights were violated when the trial court excused a prospective juror because of her beliefs about the death penalty because her affirmation that she favored the death penalty in some circumstances, specifically where the victims were children, and her responses that she could follow the law and sign the verdict form if selected as a juror because she "would have to" made it clear that excusing her for cause was error. The court of criminal appeals disagreed. Despite some inconsistencies as to her ability to follow the law regarding the death penalty, the juror's overall responses indicated her unwillingness to judge others and to return a verdict of death. In excusing her for cause, the trial court observed and noted the juror's physical responses to questioning as well as the fact that she did not equivocate regarding her answers that she was unable to sign a death verdict. The trial court had sufficient reason to believe that the juror's views about the death penalty would "prevent or substantially" impair her performance as a juror. The trial court did not err in excusing the prospective juror.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Milam

COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 199


March 17, 2009, Session 
March 3, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Milam, 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 771 (Tenn., Aug. 26, 2010)
Post-conviction relief denied at Milam v. State, 2014 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 27 (Tenn. Crim. App., Jan. 15, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Circuit Court are Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Wayne County. No. 11,016. Jim T. Hamilton, Judge.
State v. Milam, 1999 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 924 (Tenn. Crim. App., Sept. 10, 1999)



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Circuit Court are Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Wayne County (Tennessee) of first degree murder and second degree murder. Defendant was given consecutive sentences. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his first degree murder conviction. The court of criminal appeals disagreed. Defendant used a deadly weapon, a gun, to kill the unarmed victim. In addition, there was a witness who testified that defendant had threatened a few days before the murder to kill both the victim and their unborn child. There was also evidence from more than one witness that immediately after the murder, defendant went to his car, retrieved a second gun, and threw the second gun into the woods behind his house. Defendant stated that he hid the second gun because he was under the impression that it was illegal to own such a gun. Defendant had the presence of mind to try to hide something he thought to be illegal presumably because he knew the police would come to his house to investigate his wife's death. That showed calmness immediately after shooting the victim. In addition, there was testimony that the nature of the gunshot wound to the victim's forehead lead to the conclusion that the gun was pressed tightly against the victim's head when it was fired.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Watkins


No. M2009-00348-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 190


December 8, 2009, Session 
March 1, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by State v. Watkins, 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 813 (Tenn., Aug. 25, 2010)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by State v. Watkins, 2012 Tenn. LEXIS 154 (Tenn., Mar. 9, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part; Remanded. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Smith County. No. 04-194. John Wootten, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part; Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Criminal Court for Smith County (Tennessee), which convicted him of reckless homicide in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-215, and of aggravated child abuse in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-15-402(b). He was sentenced as a Range I, standard offender to four years for the reckless homicide and as a violent offender, to 25 years for aggravated child abuse, to be served consecutively.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress his statement, and in allowing the introduction of certain autopsy photographs. Upon review, the court found that defendant's previous Miranda wavier was still in effect when he made his statement as very little time had passed, he was questioned about exactly the same subject matter, and he was told several times throughout the day that he was not obligated to speak to law enforcement. In addition, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting the photographs under Tenn. R. Evid. 401, 402, and 403 because despite medical testimony describing the injuries, the photographs remained quite probative in their ability to give contest to the medical testimony. The court did find that defendant's double jeopardy rights were violated requiring merger of defendant's convictions. The evidence supporting defendant's convictions was identical, however, as it related to defendant's criminal conduct: both of his convictions rested on the same act, namely the impact he caused between the victim's head and the stairway wall in his residence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated child abuse, merged defendant's reckless homicide conviction into his aggravated child abuse conviction, and remanded for resentencing.

Moss v. State

October 21, 2009, Session 
February 24, 2010, Filed

State v. Moss, 13 S.W.3d 374, 1999 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 527 (Tenn. Crim. App., 1999)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court is Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Robertson County (Tennessee), which denied his petition for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of the second-degree murder of his wife and he currently appealed the denial of his petition for postconviction relief. The appellate court affirmed however, stating that he failed to prove that he received the ineffective assistance of counsel. The inmate argued that he received the ineffective assistance of counsel because trial counsel failed to file a motion to suppress audio tapes. However, the appellate court would not second-guess a reasonably-based trial strategy made after adequate preparation for the case. Further, the inmate failed to show that a motion to suppress would have been granted or that there was a reasonable probability that the proceedings would have concluded differently had counsel performed the suggested task. The inmate claimed that he received the ineffective assistance of counsel because appellate counsel failed to object when the trial court did not declare a mistrial or strike a portion of the prosecutor's closing argument. However, the inmate failed to point to that portion of the argument in the transcript and failed to demonstrate that the issue would have been successful on appeal.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Parker

Carr v. State


No. W2009-00683-CCA-R3-CO


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 81


November 10, 2009, Assigned on Briefs 
February 1, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 84-02112. W. Otis Higgs, Jr., Judge.
STATE v. CARR, 1985 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 3273 (Tenn. Crim. App., Oct. 30, 1985)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought judicial review of an order by the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) dismissing his petition for a writ of coram nobis. The trial court ruled the petition should be dismissed because it did not set out any newly discovered evidence and contained no exception to the one-year statute of limitations. The inmate argued that the dismissal was an unconstitutional denial of his right to due process.


OVERVIEW: The inmate had been convicted in 1984 and was serving a life sentence as a Range II offender following a conviction for aggravated rape. The inmate filed his petition for writ of error coram nobis outside the applicable statute of limitations. The State raised the time defense in its response to the petition. The inmate did not present any due process basis for tolling the statute of limitations, and he had not provided any explanation for the 20-year delay. The record was void of any reason beyond his control that prevented the timely filing of his coram nobis action. Further, the inmate acknowledged in his brief that no new evidence was alleged to exist on the face of his petition for relief. The inmate asserted that he received information pertinent to his case from the Innocence Project in 2005; therefore, he could have and should have included any claims based on that information in his petition filed in 2006. The trial court had not abused its discretion by refusing to allow an oral amendment to the petition on the day of the hearing.


OUTCOME: The trial court's dismissal was affirmed.

Coleman v. State


No. W2007-02767-CCA-R3-PD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 36


March 3, 2009, Session 
January 13, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by State v. Coleman, 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 600 (Tenn., June 17, 2010)
Affirmed in part and vacated in part by, Remanded by Coleman v. State, 341 S.W.3d 221, 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 319 (Tenn., 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. P-11326. W. Mark Ward, Judge.
State v. Coleman, 619 S.W.2d 112, 1981 Tenn. LEXIS 460 (Tenn., 1981)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of the decision of the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee), which denied his motion to reopen his postconviction petition for the limited purpose of determining whether he was mentally retarded and thus ineligible for the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: In 1980, the inmate had been convicted of first-degree felony murder and he had received a sentence of death for his role in the victim's killing. The inmate currently appealed the denial of his motion to reopen his postconviction petition for the limited purpose of determining whether he was mentally retarded and, thus, ineligible for the death penalty. The appellate court affirmed the denial of relief, stating that it was unable to conclude that the issue of the inmate's IQ was litigated at his original trial. The State never sought further prosecution or punishment of the inmate and thus, he was not placed twice in jeopardy. The appellate court was unable to conclude that the inmate manifested subaverage general intellectual functioning prior to reaching the age of 18. The inmate also failed to establish that he had adaptive deficits by a preponderance of the evidence. He failed to meet the bright-line mark of 70 for establishing mental retardation at the time of the offense and thus failed to establish by clear and convincing evidence that he was mentally retarded at the time of the offense under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-203(b) (2006).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Griffin

He was sentenced to life imprisonment and a concurrent sentence of 20 years for the robbery conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, along with two codefendants, broke into a rooming house to rob the victim, who was fatally shot. Defendant was 17 years old at the time of the crimes. A jury found defendant guilty of first-degree murder, felony murder, and especially aggravated robbery; his murder convictions were merged. OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Dorantes


No. M2007-01918-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 965


August 20, 2008, Assigned on Briefs 
November 30, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by State v. Dorantes, 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 466 (Tenn., May 13, 2010)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by State v. Dorantes, 331 S.W.3d 370, 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 8 (Tenn., 2011)
Related proceeding at State v. Patlan, 2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 89 (Tenn. Crim. App., Feb. 4, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed In Part and Reversed In Part. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 2006-D-3184. Steve R. Dozier, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed In Part and Reversed In Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), which convicted him of first degree felony murder during the perpetration of aggravated child abuse and aggravated child abuse by infliction of injury, and which sentenced him to life imprisonment for the murder and to a consecutive term of 22 years' incarceration for the aggravated child abuse conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the record was insufficient to support both his conviction for first degree felony murder based on aggravated child abuse and his conviction for aggravated child abuse, and that the trial court erred in admitting certain photographs of the victim's body. The court found that the record was devoid of any proof showing defendant inflicted physical injury upon the victim. The indictment on the aggravated child abuse count expressly provided that defendant did knowingly, other than by accidental means, treat the victim, a child six years of age or less in such a manner as to inflict injury. However, the State never argued that defendant inflicted the victim's fatal injuries and did not offer any proof in support of such theory. The evidence was sufficient to support the felony murder conviction as it showed that defendant knowingly failed to provide the victim with any medical assistance resulting in serious bodily injuries. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting autopsy photos as they were necessary to explain the medical testimony and their probative value outweighed any unfair prejudicial effect pursuant to Tenn. R. Evid. 401 and 403.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and vacated the conviction for the aggravated child abuse, modified defendant's sentence to life imprisonment, and affirmed the felony murder conviction.

Bailey v. State


No. E2009-00203-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 910


September 22, 2009, Assigned on Briefs 
November 3, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Bailey v. State, 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 418 (Tenn., Apr. 23, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Hamilton County. No. 270239. Rebecca J. Stern, Judge.
State v. Bailey, 2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 993 (Tenn. Crim. App., Dec. 27, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of the decision of the Criminal Court for Hamilton County (Tennessee), which dismissed his petition for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The inmate appealed from the postconviction court's summarily dismissing his petition for postconviction relief as time-barred. The appellate court affirmed however, stating that it agreed that the petition was untimely. The petition was required to have been filed within a year of the final action of the highest state appellate court to which an appeal was taken pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-102(a). Regardless of any administrative alteration of the judgment within the Tennessee Offender Management Information System system, the inmate's application for permission to appeal was denied by the supreme court on April 23, 2007. Thus, the statute clearly mandated that any filing past April 23, 2008, was untimely. Further, the petition presented no argument that would have excused the late-filing of the petition. The inmate's grounds for relief addressed issues disposed of on direct appeal of his criminal case. The postconviction court did not err by failing to hold a hearing or appoint counsel; it had no jurisdiction to hear the petition, and it correctly ordered a summary dismissal.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Humphrey v. State


No. M2008-01069-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 816


February 10, 2009, Session 
September 29, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Humphrey v. State, 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 253 (Tenn., Mar. 15, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court is Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for White County. No. CR815. David Patterson, Judge.
State v. Humphrey, 2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 924 (Tenn. Crim. App., Aug. 24, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court is Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of a judgment from the Criminal Court for White County (Tennessee), which denied his petition for post-conviction relief after he was convicted of second degree murder.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued that trial counsel was ineffective because he failed to effectively cross-examine the inmate's wife, failed to object to the State's comparison of the inmate's treatment of his wife to that of Osama Bin Laden's, and failed to challenged the constitutionality of Tennessee's sentencing law. On appeal, the court determined that the failure to extensively cross-examine the wife was a reasonably-based trial strategy in a case where the wife and the inmate had widely varying stories as to the facts and the two were the only eyewitnesses to the crime. The inmate was unable to show that counsel was either ineffective in his cross-examination or that he was prejudiced by the cross-examination. In addition, trial counsel's decision not to object to the Bin Laden comparison was a tactical decision made during the course of the proceedings and thus, trial counsel was not ineffective. Finally, the court held that trial counsel was not ineffective for failing to raise the sentencing law issue because there was no basis to raise it and the inmate did not prove that there was a reasonable probability that he would have been successful on the issue on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the petition.

State v. Anderson


No. M2008-01377-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 823


June 9, 2009, Session 
September 28, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Anderson, 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 254 (Tenn., Mar. 15, 2010)
Decision reached on appeal by State v. Anderson, 2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 38 (Tenn. Crim. App., Jan. 20, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part; Remanded. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 2006-C-2268. Monte Watkins, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part; Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), which convicted him of five counts of statutory rape in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-506 (2005), and two counts of assault in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-101.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that trial counsel erred in allowing the victim to testify regarding four instances of digital penetration and one instance of cunnilingus. The court concluded that the trial court did not err in admitting such testimony because the victim did not contradict herself and that the victim understood the questions asked of her. In addition, defendant challenged the sufficiency of the evidence with regard to his convictions. The court held that consent was a complete defense to assault under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-101 and that thus, because defendant digitally penetrated the victim with her consent, the assault convictions had to be vacated. The evidence, however, was sufficient to sustain the statutory rape convictions as the victim was 13 during the time period at issue, and the victim testified that defendant committed each of the charged acts. Finally, defendant challenged his sentence. The court determined that because the trial court's order of one year of day-for-day of confinement was far less that the possible 2.4 years, the sentence was authorized by Tennessee sentencing law, although that the sentence was to be served day-for-day was contrary to law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for statutory rape, vacated his convictions for assault, affirmed his sentence length and split confinement, remanded and ordered the sentencing that judgment forms correctly reflected service of his period of confinement, and ordered that the day-for-day service requirement be deleted.

 

488 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Nuby v. State


No. W2008-02554-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 850


September 1, 2009, Assigned on Briefs 
September 25, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Reversed and Remanded. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 02-02068. Paula Skahan, Judge.
State v. Nuby, 2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 156 (Tenn. Crim. App., Feb. 21, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought judicial review of the Criminal Court for Shelby County's (Tennessee) dismissal of his petition for post-conviction relief as untimely and later attempt to vacate the order of dismissal. He argued that dismissal was in error because his petition was timely filed and that the post-conviction court did not have jurisdiction to vacate its order because the order had become final.


OVERVIEW: The inmate first argued that the post-conviction court erred in summarily dismissing his petition for post-conviction relief as untimely. The State agreed that the post-conviction court erred because the petition was filed within one year of the denial of his application for permission to appeal to the Tennessee Supreme Court. The record established that the Tennessee Supreme Court denied the inmate's application for permission to appeal on June 18, 2007. He filed his petition for post-conviction relief on April 3, 2008. Thus, the inmate was clearly within the time frame for filing, and the post-conviction court erred in summarily dismissing his petition as outside the one-year statute of limitations. The State also agreed with the inmate that the post-conviction court lacked jurisdiction to vacate its dismissal of his petition for post-conviction relief. The post-conviction court's May 1, 2008, summary dismissal of the petition became final on May 31, 2008. Therefore, the post-conviction court was without jurisdiction to vacate its order of dismissal on November 13, 2008.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the post-conviction court was reversed, and the case was remanded to that court for proceedings in accordance with the Post-Conviction Procedure Act.

 

489 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Burks v. Lindamood


No. M2009-00071-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 805


August 19, 2009, Assigned on Briefs 
September 24, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Wayne County. No. 14512. Jim T. Hamilton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Wayne County (Tennessee), which summarily dismissed his petition for habeas corpus relief.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued that the habeas corpus statute, Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-21-109, was an unconstitutional suspension of the writ and that the State was illegally depriving him of his inalienable right to his liberty by permitting slavery as punishment for crime. Upon review, the court held that notwithstanding any potential procedural waiver, as asserted by the State, dismissal for failing to state a cognizable ground for habeas relief was also correct. Although the consecutive or concurrent nature of his sentences was not entirely clear from the attachments submitted by the inmate, the inmate did not provide the court with sufficient documentation to substantiate his claim that his sentence was illegal or had expired. Most of the documentation provided by the inmate was in agreement that some consecutive service of his sentences was ordered. The court lacked sufficient information to determine the effective length of the inmate's sentences; regardless, it did not appear that any effective sentence would have expired. The inmate's confinement resulted from his commission of criminal acts and was not equivalent to slavery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order summarily dismissing the petition.

 

490 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Smart v. State


No. M2009-00651-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 806


August 19, 2009, Assigned on Briefs 
September 23, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 2001-A-162. J. Randall Wyatt, Jr., Judge.
State v. Smart, 2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 418 (Tenn. Crim. App., May 13, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of an order from the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), which summarily dismissed his petition for habeas corpus relief under Tenn. Const. art. I, § 15.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued that the trial court was without jurisdiction to sentence him because: (1) in refusing to allow the jury to be informed of the punishment for first degree murder, the trial judge applied a procedure which was appropriate under Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 40-35-101 to -505, but not under the first degree sentencing procedures, Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 39-13-202 to -208, and thus, the trial judge created a third procedure or act which was not legislatively authorized; and (2) Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-208(c) unconstitutionally transferred the sentencing power to the executive branch. The court agreed with the habeas corpus court that the inmate merely submitted conclusory legal abstractions. The court found no need to become bogged down analyzing such abstractions. The inmate did not provide the court with any authority, and the court knew of none, that the two statutes could not work in conjunction with one another. Finally, the inmate's lawful sentence had not expired, and the sentencing court had jurisdiction and authority to enter the judgment against him. Because the petition did not state a cognizable claim for habeas corpus relief, summary dismissal was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order summarily dismissing the petition.

State v. Gilliam


No. W2007-02401-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 797


December 2, 2008, Session 
September 22, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected March 8, 2010.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 06-06976. Chris Craft, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee), which convicted him of theft of property valued at over $ 1,000 in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-14-103, -105(3) (2003), felon in possession of a handgun, leaving the scene of an accident resulting in injury, and driving on a suspended license.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient for the theft conviction, and that the trial court erred by providing the jury with an improper instruction on reasonable doubt and by finding that defendant's 2007 conviction for aggravated robbery was admissible for impeachment under Tenn. R. Evid. 609. The court found that although the victim's girlfriend had legal title to the vehicle that was stolen, she testified that the victim would borrow the vehicle from time to time because they bought the vehicle together, and that the victim borrowed her the vehicle on the night of the offense. Thereby the definition of owner under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-11-106(a)(26) was satisfied and the evidence was sufficient to support the theft of property conviction. Defendant was not entitled to relief regarding the jury instruction under plain error review because a clear and unequivocal rule of law was not breached. Finally, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting the 2007 conviction because defendant in fact had nine convictions for aggravated robbery which were extremely relevant to his credibility, and the prejudicial effect was limited by admitting only one conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Phelps


No. M2008-01096-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 757


July 21, 2009, Assigned on Briefs 
September 10, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by State v. Phelps, 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 157 (Tenn., Mar. 15, 2010)
Reversed by, Remanded by, Motion granted by State v. Phelps, 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 1150 (Tenn., Dec. 16, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Bedford County. No. 16428. F. Lee Russell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Bedford County (Tennessee), which denied his motion to withdraw his guilty plea and sentenced him to three years in the Tennessee Department of Correction (TDOC) as a Range II offender. He had pled guilty to violating the sex offender registry due to the failure to register a change of residence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to charges of violating the sex offender registry statute due to failure to register a change of residence. Before the sentencing hearing, defendant filed a motion to withdraw his guilty plea, which the trial court denied. The trial court sentenced him to three years in the TDOC and he appealed. The appellate court affirmed. The transcript from the guilty plea hearing confirmed that the trial court thoroughly explained the nature of the charge defendant faced, the consequences of an open plea, and the rights defendant waived by pleading guilty. The trial court repeatedly asked defendant if he understood the guilty plea, to which he always answered affirmatively. Thus, there was no error in the refusal to all him to withdraw his guilty plea. In regard to his sentence, under T.C.A. § 40-35-106(b)(4), the trial court properly considered the two felony convictions separately for sentencing purposes and properly found defendant a Range II multiple offender. Defendant's argument involving the further enhancement of his sentence was waived for failing to argue or cite authority in support of that argument.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Hardy


No. M2008-00381-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 727


November 20, 2008, Session 
August 31, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at Hardy v. State, 2012 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 14 (Tenn. Crim. App., Jan. 9, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Circuit Court are Affirmed in Part, Modified in Part, and the Case is Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Rutherford County. No. F-58763C. Joseph Dailey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Circuit Court are Affirmed in Part, Modified in Part, and the Case is Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Rutherford County (Tennessee), which convicted him of first degree premeditated murder, first degree felony murder, especially aggravated robbery, aggravated burglary, conspiracy to commit especially aggravated robbery, and conspiracy to commit especially aggravated burglary.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the admission of his statement on the grounds that police violated the constitutional rights of his co-defendant, when they obtained the co-defendant's statement implicating defendant, and on the grounds that it was not voluntary. The court held that defendant lacked standing to assert the violation of his co-defendant's constitutional rights under U.S. Const. amend. IV and U.S. Const. amend. V. Defendant's attempt to circumvent his lack of standing by framing his argument in terms of his own due process rights failed as there was no evidence to indicate that police used the co-defendant's statement in any way to violate defendant's due process rights. Defendant's rights under U.S. Const. amend. V and Tenn. Const. art. I, § 9 were not violated because defendant's confession was voluntary as he was aware of his rights and remained aware thereof throughout the continuous interrogation. Finally, under Double Jeopardy Clauses of the United States and Tennessee Constitutions, and Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-12-103(c), the two conspiracy convictions should have be merged into a single conviction of conspiracy to commit especially aggravated robbery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Perez


No. E2008-01391-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 715


March 24, 2009, Session 
August 25, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Perez, 2009 Tenn. LEXIS 874 (Tenn., Dec. 21, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court is Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Hamblen County. No. 07CR489. John Dugger, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court is Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Criminal Court for Hamblen County (Tennessee), which convicted him of aggravated kidnapping in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-304(a)(1), a Class B Felony, and which sentenced him to 10 years as a violent offender.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress his statement, the aggravated kidnapping statute was unconstitutional, there was insufficient evidence to support his conviction, and his sentence was excessive. The court found that the evidence did not preponderate against the trial court's findings that defendant was fluent in both English and Spanish and that defendant voluntarily executed both a consent to search and a Miranda waiver. Thus, the motion to suppress was properly denied. The court also found no constitutional requirement that defendant be separately charged and convicted of an underlying felony in order to hold sufficient evidence supporting the primary felony and thus, the indictment was not based upon an unconstitutional statute. The victim testified that defendant grabbed her, forced her into his car, prevented her from escaping, pushed her down onto a bed, and forced her to have sex. Such evidence was sufficient to support the conviction. Finally, the record reflected that the trial court followed the applicable sentencing principles and appropriately found the existence of applicable enhancement factors and mitigating factors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Fair


No. W2007-00730-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 670


October 7, 2008, Assigned on Briefs 
August 14, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Fair, 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 215 (Tenn., Feb. 22, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 04-02746. James C. Beasley, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Two defendants sought review of the decision of the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee), which convicted them of aggravated robbery in violation of T.C.A. § 39-13-402(a)(1). They were both sentenced as a Range II, multiple offender, to 18 years.


OVERVIEW: Both defendants were convicted of aggravated robbery; the appellate court affirmed. The first defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to dismiss the indictment against him on the basis of prosecutorial vindictiveness. He contended that his re-indictment on the greater charge of aggravated robbery after he decided not to accept the State's offer of settlement based on a charge of facilitation of aggravated robbery created a presumption of vindictiveness. However, he failed to point to any vindictiveness. The newly assigned prosecutor decided that the circumstances supported an indictment of aggravated robbery under a theory of criminal responsibility. The trial court did not err in allowing a weapon found in the apartment of defendant's roommate to have been introduced into evidence. The victim testified that an AK-47 rifle was used during the offense and an AK-47 rifle was found in the first defendant's apartment after the robbery. The evidence was relevant and any discrepancy between the victim's description at trial of the weapon used during the robbery and the actual weapon recovered went to the weight the jury might have chosen to assign the evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Armstrong v. State


No. M2008-01818-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 641


March 17, 2009, Assigned on Briefs 
August 11, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Armstrong v. State, 2009 Tenn. LEXIS 768 (Tenn., Nov. 23, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court is Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Marshall County. No. 08CR44. Lee Russell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court is Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Marshall County (Tennessee), which denied his motion for post-conviction relief. Defendant had pleaded guilty to two counts of selling cocaine weighing in excess of.5 gram, both Class B felonies, and one count of selling cocaine weighing less than.5 gram, a Class C felony.


OVERVIEW: The inmate claimed that he received ineffective assistance of counsel, that his guilty plea was involuntarily entered, that the post-conviction statute Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-110(f) was unconstitutional, and that he was sentenced in violation of Blakely v. Washington. On appeal, the court found that the inmate failed to establish that he received ineffective assistance of counsel because he did not present potential witnesses that counsel did not locate at the post-conviction hearing. Further, the inmate failed to show that had counsel located the witnesses he would have insisted on going to trial. In addition, the inmate failed to show that his plea was not voluntary or intelligent as the inmate was made aware of the consequences of pleading guilty, the inmate understood the plea agreement, and the inmate understood his rights and the sentence he would receive. Further, the inmate waived the issue pertaining to the constitutionality of the statute as it was not addressed with the post-conviction court. Finally, the sentence violation issue had no merit as Blakely id no apply retroactively to cases that were on collateral appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

497 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Simmons


No. M2008-00107-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 624


October 7, 2008, Session 
August 5, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed and Vacated. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Van Buren County. No. 2054F. Larry B. Stanley, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed and Vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Van Buren County, Tennessee, that convicted him of the promotion of methamphetamine manufacture, arguing that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence because his detention exceeded the constitutionally lawful period for a detention under U.S. Const. amend. IV and Tenn. Const. art. I, § 7, and that his consent to search was invalid.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped for not wearing a seat belt in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-9-603(a)(2) (2006). Although defendant refused to consent to a search of his vehicle, he subsequently gave consent to a second deputy who arrived on the scene, and a search uncovered illegal drugs. On review, the court held that the deputy detained defendant and his passengers based solely on their nervous behavior and his knowledge of their past criminal involvement with methamphetamine. This was constitutionally insufficient to constitute reasonable suspicion to extend the detention. Further, where the deputy admitted that he generally issued a traffic citation within 10 minutes of stopping a vehicle but had not begun to write a citation related to this stop and asked for consent to search 15 minutes after making the traffic stop, the length of the detention exceeded that allowed under the cite and release statute, Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 40-7-118 and 55-10-207. Because the detention was excessive and illegal and because the consent to search was not sufficiently attenuated from the illegal detention, defendant's consent was not voluntary, and his motion to suppress should have been granted.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

498 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kemp


No. M2008-01624-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 609


May 12, 2009, Session 
July 31, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at State v. Kemp, 2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 277 (Tenn. Crim. App., Apr. 18, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part; Remanded. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Smith County. No. 05-234. John Wootten, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part; Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Smith County, Tennessee, that convicted him of three counts of vehicular homicide by recklessness and three counts of reckless endangerment with a deadly weapon in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 39-13-213(b)(1) and 39-13-103(b), arguing that the evidence was insufficient to support his convictions.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court held that the evidence was sufficient to convict defendant because it showed that defendant, while under the influence of cocaine, chased after the victims' vehicle and, at four separate times, hit it hard enough to cause debris to fall into the road, with the final impact occurring immediately before the crash site. At that time, the victims' car had been moving fast enough that the left edges of both driver's side tires left markings on the road as the car skidded to the right and into to a ditch. Those facts permitted a rational jury to disbelieve defendant's account of a low-speed chase featuring slight accidental contact and to believe that defendant hit the victims' car having consciously disregarded any danger of death or serious injury. However, the trial court erred in finding the consecutive sentencing statute, Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-115, unconstitutional and imposing consecutive sentences under its inherent powers; Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-115(b) required certain findings to be made before imposing consecutive sentences. Finally, the failure to merge each pair of convictions violated double jeopardy because they arose from the same criminal conduct.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed, but the case was remanded for reconsideration of the consecutive sentences and for entry of judgment forms properly reflecting merger of the reckless endangerment convictions into the vehicular homicide convictions.

State v. Sweet


No. E2008-00100-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 591


November 18, 2008, Session 
July 21, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Knox County. No. 84829. Mary Beth Leibowitz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the sentences imposed by the Criminal Court for Knox County, Tennessee, following his convictions for vehicular homicide by intoxication and vehicular assault by intoxication, arguing that the trial court erred in imposing consecutive sentences under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-115(b)(4) (2006).


OVERVIEW: On review, the court held that the record supported the imposition of consecutive sentences for defendant's convictions of vehicular homicide by intoxication and vehicular assault by intoxication on the basis that defendant was a dangerous offender because the record showed that defendant developed a drinking problem as early as two years before the accident and, throughout this time, friends and family members tried to convince defendant to enter a treatment facility to address his drinking issues; that defendant refused to treat his alcohol dependence; that, six months prior to the accident at issue, defendant was convicted of driving drunk in Texas but that this did not curb defendant's drinking; and that, on the day at issue, defendant consumed a significant amount of alcohol before beginning his drive home to pick up his children, swerved into the opposite lane, and struck the victims' vehicle, killing one victim and severely injuring the other. By rejecting intervention efforts, continuing to drink after his Texas D.U.I. conviction, and, ultimately, drunkenly making his way home to pick up his children, defendant created a situation where the risk to human life was high.


OUTCOME: The sentences imposed by the trial court were affirmed.

Transou v. State


No. W2008-02713-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 537



July 9, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion denied by Transou v. State, 2009 Tenn. LEXIS 808 (Tenn., Nov. 23, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20 of the Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Madison County. No. C-08-330. Roy Morgan, Judge.
State v. Transou, 2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 664 (Tenn. Crim. App., June 30, 2005)
State v. Transou, 2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 463 (Tenn. Crim. App., May 13, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed. Pursuant to Rule 20 of the Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed a judgment of the Madison County Circuit Court, Tennessee, which dismissed his petition for writ of habeas corpus. The State moved to affirm the judgment pursuant to Tenn. Ct. Crim. App. R. 20.


OVERVIEW: The State asserted that petitioner did not comply with the procedural requirements of Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-21-107 because the affidavit attached to the petition was not notarized, petitioner failed to state that the legality of his confinement had not already been adjudged, and the petition was not filed in the appropriate county. Moreover, the State argued that the collection of petitioner's DNA has previously been adjudicated on direct appeal or in prior habeas actions and should not be relitigated. The instant court concluded that petitioner was not entitled to habeas corpus relief. Petitioner offered as an affidavit a document that was not notarized. As such, it was insufficient to satisfy the affidavit requirement of the habeas corpus statute. The habeas court's summary dismissal of the petition was proper because the petition failed to comply with the procedural requirements of habeas corpus relief. Next, though not entirely clear from petitioner's brief, to the extent that he argued the collection of his DNA was improper or unconstitutional, the instant court concluded that this issue had been previously adjudicated, and therefore without merit.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

501 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Cribbs v. State


No. W2006-01381-CCA-R3-PD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 524


March 4, 2008, Session 
July 1, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Cribbs v. State, 2009 Tenn. LEXIS 881 (Tenn., Dec. 21, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court is Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part, and the Case is Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. P-20670. Carolyn Blackett, Judge.
State v. Cribbs, 967 S.W.2d 773, 1998 Tenn. LEXIS 207 (Tenn., 1998)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court is Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part, and the Case is Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed a judgment of the Criminal Court of Shelby County, Tennessee, that denied his petition for post-conviction relief following his convictions for first-degree murder, attempted first-degree murder, and aggravated burglary, arguing that counsel was ineffective in failing to make inquiry into his mental impairments.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court held that, where petitioner's I.Q. was determined to be 70 when he was 13, 73 when he was 19, and 75 when he was 28, the post-conviction court did not err in finding that petitioner failed to show by a preponderance of the evidence that he was mentally retarded, as the legislature intended for a score of 70 to be the bright-line cutoff and did not take into account standard rates of error. However, petitioner's attorneys were ineffective in failing to investigate petitioner's mental impairment where they were aware that he had some type of mental impairment; because petitioner was charged with first-degree murder and the State was seeking a capital sentence, the failure to investigate prevented counsel from discovering that petitioner had an I.Q. test when he was 13 years old that revealed him to have an I.Q. of 70, which was the threshold delineating mental retardation and ineligibility for the death penalty under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-203. Even if the trial court would have found that petitioner was not mentally retarded, defense counsel could nevertheless have presented this evidence to the to show mitigating circumstances.


OUTCOME: The sentence of death was reversed, and the case was remanded for a new sentencing hearing, but the judge who presided over the post-conviction proceeding was disqualified from any subsequent proceedings. With regard to the guilt phase of the trial, the judgment of the post-conviction court was affirmed.

O'Quinn v. State


No. E2008-02728-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 519


May 19, 2009, Assigned on Briefs 
June 22, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by O'Quinn v. State, 2009 Tenn. LEXIS 690 (Tenn., Oct. 19, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Washington County. Nos. 17527, 17999. Lynn W. Brown, Judge.
O'Quinn v. Carlton, 1998 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 171 (Tenn. Crim. App., Feb. 6, 1998)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed the judgment of the Criminal Court for Washington County, Tennessee, denying his petitions for post-conviction relief and writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: In 2008, petitioner filed petitions for post-conviction relief and for habeas corpus relief from 1989 guilty-pleaded convictions of two counts of aggravated rape. Petitioner claimed he was denied the effective assistance of counsel and that his persistent offender sentence was illegal. Petitioner acknowledged that his petition for post-conviction relief had been filed outside the applicable three-year statute of limitations. However, his bare allegation that due process principles required the tolling of the statute of limitations was insufficient to trigger further inquiry. Petitioner's claim that the trial court enhanced his sentence in violation of Blakely did not avail him habeas corpus relief, because he was sentenced 15 years before the decision. His claim that he was denied the effective assistance of counsel at trial and that his guilty pleas were unknowingly and involuntarily entered did not present cognizable grounds for habeas corpus relief. The Court of Criminal Appeals of Tennessee upheld the trial court's decision denying the petitions without an evidentiary hearing.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Jordan


No. W2007-01272-CCA-R3-DD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 455


September 9, 2008, Session 
June 9, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by State v. Jordan, 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 874 (Tenn., Sept. 22, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Madison County. No. 05-431. Roy B. Morgan, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Madison County that convicted him of first-degree premeditated murder, first-degree felony murder, attempted first-degree murder, aggravated assault, and leaving the scene of an accident and that imposed a capital sentence.


OVERVIEW: Armed with numerous weapons and ammunition, defendant drove to his estranged wife's workplace, shot his wife in the leg to "get her attention," shot her three more times after she fell to the floor, and shot three other victims before leaving and returning with additional fire power and firing numerous additional shots into his wife's lifeless body. On review, the court held that aggravating factor under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-204(i)(5) was proper because the wife's murder was atrocious and cruel. The wounds to the victim's head inflicted in the initial shooting were fatal; as such, the additional wounds inflicted were beyond that necessary to cause death. The Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-204(i)(12) mass murder aggravating factor was also proper because defendant killed three people during the shooting. In conducting its proportionality and reasonableness review under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-206, the court found the death penalty to be reasonable; the death penalty had been upheld in numerous cases where the victim was the defendant's wife or girlfriend, in cases in which the defendant committed mass murder, and in which the defendant had little or no prior criminal history.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

Dean v. Easterling


No. W2008-01302-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 386



May 22, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hardeman County. No. 08-02-0323. Joe Walker, III, Judge.
State v. Dean, 76 S.W.3d 352, 2001 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 791 (Tenn. Crim. App., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Hardeman County, Tennessee, denying his petition for habeas corpus relief.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted by a jury of aggravated rape. The trial court sentenced petitioner, as a violent offender, to forty years confinement. He filed unsuccessful motions for post-conviction and habeas relief. Petitioner filed a second petition for habeas corpus relief, alleging that his conviction was void due to the fact that his initial detention was unconstitutional and therefore all subsequent trial proceedings were void. The trial court summarily dismissed the petition, finding that petitioner's sentence had not expired and that the trial court had jurisdiction to enter the judgment against petitioner. The Court of Criminal Appeals of Tennessee upheld the decision. The trial court, by virtue of a valid indictment issued after the arrest and detention, was vested with subject matter jurisdiction to adjudicate petitioner's guilt. The claims raised by petitioner has been previously determined and could not be re-litigated in a habeas petition. Petitioner's claim that his due process rights were violated as a result of an unconstitutional detention was not a cognizable claim for habeas corpus relief.


OUTCOME: The State's motion was granted, and the judgment of the habeas court was affirmed in accordance with Tenn. R. Ct. Crim. App. 20.

 

505 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wiggins


No. W2007-01734-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 353


September 9, 2008, Assigned on Briefs 
May 15, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended September 14, 2009.
Appeal denied by State v. Wiggins, 2009 Tenn. LEXIS 877 (Tenn., Dec. 21, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Circuit Court are Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Dyer County. No. C06-248. Russell Lee Moore, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Circuit Court are Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dyer County, Tennessee, that convicted him of selling cocaine within a drug-free school zone under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-17-417(a)(3), arguing that the Drug-Free School Zone Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-17-432 (2005), was unconstitutional because it violated due process and arguing that the trial court erred in failing to instruct the jury on the lesser-included offense of facilitation.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court held that the Drug-Free School Zone Act was not overbroad or vague and did not violate the principles of due process. Although the language of the 2005 amendment was poorly worded, the act's subsections were not contradictory or vague. Because defendant sold cocaine within 1,000 feet of a school, he was subject to an enhanced penalty. Further, the trial court did not err in refusing to instruct the jury on facilitation as a lesser-included offense of selling cocaine. The evidence did not support a jury instruction on facilitation under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-11-403(a) as a lesser-included offense because the evidence established that a confidential informant telephoned defendant, that she told the person who answered that she wanted to buy cocaine, and that defendant arrived at the informant's location and sold cocaine to her. Although the defense theorized that defendant merely delivered the drugs for the person who answered the phone, the evidence, not the theories of the parties, controlled whether an instruction was required.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

Rogers v. State


No. E2008-01324-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 348


March 25, 2009, Assigned on Briefs 
May 14, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Cumberland County. No. 8725. Leon C. Burns, Jr., Judge.
Rogers v. Lindamood, 2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 971 (Tenn. Crim. App., Dec. 12, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of a judgment from the Criminal Court for Cumberland County (Tennessee), which denied his petition for post-conviction relief in which he challenged his conviction of attempted aggravated child neglect of a child less than six years old.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued that his counsel was ineffective and his plea was not voluntary. Respondent State of Tennessee argued that the petition was untimely as it exceeded the one-year statute of limitations under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-102(b). In reply, the inmate asserted post-conviction court erred in dismissing his petition as untimely because the statute of limitations for filing was tolled by the unconstitutional failure of another county's circuit court to treat his petition for habeas corpus relief, as one for post-conviction relief. The court found that the inmate's habeas corpus petition was filed in the other county, where he was imprisoned, and such was not the county where he was originally convicted as required under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-104(a). The other county's circuit court had no jurisdiction to hear the inmate's post-conviction claims because it did not enter the judgment of conviction, and it had no authority to transfer the case to the conviction county. During the entire litigation of his habeas corpus claim, the inmate never argued that his non-cognizable claims should be treated as post-conviction claims for purposes of Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-105(c).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Brotherton


No. W2007-02016-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 298


July 1, 2008, Session 
April 23, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by State v. Brotherton, 2009 Tenn. LEXIS 632 (Tenn., Sept. 28, 2009)
Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Brotherton, 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 878 (Tenn., Sept. 27, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed and Dismissed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Carroll County. No. 07CR66. Donald E. Parish, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed and Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Carroll County (Tennessee), which convicted him after he pled guilty to the offense of driving under the influence, first offense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to the offense of driving under the influence, first offense, and reserved a certified question of law regarding the validity of the traffic stop that resulted in his arrest. The appellate court reversed and dismissed the indictment, stating that the trooper lacked reasonable suspicion to make the traffic stop. The taillight was broken, but an attempt to repair the light had been made by defendant. Applying those facts to the taillight statute, Tennessee Code Annotated section 55-9-402, the officer did not have probable cause to believe the taillight was not in "good condition." The taillight on the vehicle driven by defendant was not in perfect condition nor was it in pristine condition. Rather, it was in working condition. The trooper testified that the taillight was operational and was not a safety issue to anyone on the night that he stopped the defendant. Having a light covered largely in red tape was not the optimum situation, but defendant did make an attempt to maintain his vehicle in proper working order.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the judgment and dismissed the indictment.

509 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brown


No. M2007-00427-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 301


July 22, 2008, Session 
April 20, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Brown, 2009 Tenn. LEXIS 648 (Tenn., Sept. 28, 2009)
Post-conviction relief denied at Brown v. State, 2014 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1014 (Tenn. Crim. App., Nov. 6, 2014)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Dismissed by, Certificate of appealability denied Brown v. Freeman, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 150493 (M.D. Tenn., Oct. 28, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 2005-A-215. J. Randall Wyatt, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Criminal Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, that convicted her of first-degree premeditated murder and first-degree felony murder under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-202 (2003) and especially aggravated robbery under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-403 (2003), arguing that the evidence was insufficient to support her convictions.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court held that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction of first-degree premeditated murder because defendant carried a handgun in her purse when she arrived at the victim's house and, once inside the victim's bedroom, pulled the gun from her purse and shot the victim. While defendant argued self-defense, there was no evidence that the victim was armed; no other weapon was found in the victim's bedroom and the victim's fingers were locked beneath his head when he was found by police. Further, defendant admitted to police that the victim did not try to force himself on her and did not threaten her with a gun at any point. The evidence also supported felony murder and aggravated robbery convictions because defendant killed the victim before taking his guns, which she intended to pawn, and cash. While defendant robbed the victim after killing him, the sequence of events did not foreclose a felony murder conviction because defendant took the victim's guns and money immediately after she killed him; this established a sufficient connection of time, place, and continuity of action to show that the killing occurred in perpetration of the robbery.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for especially aggravated robbery was reversed, and the case was remanded for entry of a judgment of conviction for aggravated robbery, the offense with which defendant was charged, and for imposition of a sentence on that offense. In all other respects, the judgment of conviction was affirmed.

State v. Webb


No. W2008-00094-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 265


December 2, 2008, Assigned on Briefs 
April 16, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Webb v. State, 2009 Tenn. LEXIS 633 (Tenn., Sept. 28, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 03-06789. Lee V. Coffee, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) of two counts of robbery, two counts of aggravated robbery, and one count of intentionally evading arrest. After merger of the robbery and aggravated robbery convictions, defendant was sentenced as a Range I offender to twelve years imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that his statement to law enforcement was not voluntary. The court of appeals disagreed. The evidence showed that before giving his statement, defendant was advised of his rights twice, and twice indicated he understood those rights. The evidence also showed that defendant was not threatened or coerced, and that at the time that he gave a statement, defendant did not appear to be under the influence of crack cocaine. Additionally, defendant testified that he had attended three years of college and had experience with the judicial system. Defendant stated that at the time of the interview, he understood that he did not have to give a statement to the police and could have an attorney present. The trial court's findings that defendant was read and understood his Miranda rights, voluntarily signed a waiver of those rights, was not threatened, and was not under the influence of any intoxicant at the time he gave a statement were supported by the record and were presumed correct. Therefore, the evidence did not preponderate against the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
