State v. Pearson


No. M2007-02257-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 275


October 7, 2008, Assigned on Briefs 
April 6, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed and Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Montgomery County. No. 40500314. John H. Gasaway, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of the decision of the Criminal Court for Montgomery County (Tennessee), which granted a motion to suppress evidence seized as a result of a warrantless arrest and search of defendant.


OVERVIEW: The State appealed the trial court's grant of a motion to suppress the evidence seized as a result of a warrantless arrest and subsequent search of defendant. The appellate court concluded that the police officers had probable cause to arrest and search defendant. Accordingly, the appellate court reversed and remanded the judgment. While conducting surveillance of a suspected drug dealer, the officer observed defendant give money to the suspected drug dealer in exchange for a small plastic bag. Given his law enforcement experience, the officer interpreted the exchange as an illegal drug transaction and relayed his observations to other police officers. Based on the officer's firsthand observations, defendant was ultimately arrested and told by police while in custody that he was going to be searched. The officer's observations satisfied the probable cause standard for a warrantless arrest; accordingly, the eventual search after defendant's arrest was constitutionally sound as a search incident to a lawful arrest under the Fourth Amendment to the United States Constitution and Article I, section 7 of the Tennessee Constitution.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the judgment that granted the motion to suppress and remanded for further proceedings.

 

515 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Bland v. State


No. W2007-00020-CCA-R3-PD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 283


April 8, 2008, Session 
April 3, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. P-20147. W. Fred Axley, Judge.
State v. Bland, 958 S.W.2d 651, 1997 Tenn. LEXIS 587 (Tenn., Dec. 1, 1997)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed a judgment of the Criminal Court for Shelby County that denied his petition for post-conviction relief following his convictions of first-degree murder, attempted first-degree murder, especially aggravated robbery, and attempted aggravated robbery, arguing that his trial counsel was ineffective.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court held that, although appointed counsel did not meet the American Bar Association (ABA) standards for capital representation, those guidelines were not binding upon Tennessee, and there was no authority that the ABA's qualifications for capital counsel or the required qualifications for capital counsel in Tenn. Sup. Ct. R. 13 were constitutionally compelled. The Fourteenth Amendment guidelines simply required the appointment of an attorney to a capital defendant; that counsel failed to meet the heightened requirements of Tenn. Sup. Ct. R. 13 did not render her representation per se ineffective. Further, counsel was not ineffective for failing to request a jury instruction on the defense of ignorance or mistake of fact under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-11-502 (2003) and Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-11-203 (2003). Although defendant claimed that he did not intend to kill the victim because he shot at his legs, the facts established that defendant chased the victim underneath a vehicle and then fired multiple rounds at the victim's legs; when defendant employed a deadly weapon against another in a deadly manner, it could only be concluded that he intended a deadly result.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the post-conviction court was affirmed.

State v. Hodge


No. M2007-00940-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 208


August 20, 2008, Assigned on Briefs 
March 25, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part and Modified in Part. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Lawrence County. No. 24246. Stella L. Hargrove, Judge.
State v. Hodge, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 292 (Tenn., Apr. 3, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part and Modified in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Lawrence County, Tennessee, that convicted her of theft of property valued over $60,000 in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-14-103 and imposed a 10-year term of imprisonment, arguing that the evidence was insufficient to support her conviction and that the trial court erred in imposing an excessive sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant worked at a hospital until it was discovered that she was embezzling money. On review of her conviction, the court held that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction because the State not only proved her guilt through the use of her confession but also through the use of records and bank statements that defendant embezzled over $174,000 by altering checks originally made payable to insurance companies by making herself the payee and by stealing cash from the hospital's bank deposits. The State proved defendant's theft by comparing the carbon copies of checks as they first appeared with the altered checks listing defendant as the payee at the time they were presented at the bank and then systematically showed that defendant endorsed these checks and then contemporaneously cashed or deposited them into her joint bank account shared by her husband; the State also showed contemporaneous deposits of cash that corresponded to the cash missing from the hospital's bank deposits. However, the trial court committed a Blakely violation by applying enhancement factors that were not found by a jury beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed, but the sentence was modified by reducing it to the presumptive sentence of eight years.

State v. Crump


No. M2006-02244-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 200


March 18, 2008, Session 
March 18, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Crump, 2009 Tenn. LEXIS 546 (Tenn., Aug. 24, 2009)
Post-conviction relief denied at Crump v. State, 2012 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 580 (Tenn. Crim. App., Aug. 3, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 2004-D-3137. Walter C. Kurtz, Judge.
State v. Crump, 834 S.W.2d 265, 1992 Tenn. LEXIS 358 (Tenn., 1992)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) of, inter alia, first degree premeditated murder, first degree felony murder based upon the predicate crime of rape, and first degree felony murder based upon the predicate crime of larceny. Defendant was sentenced to life imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his felony murder and premeditated murder convictions. The court of criminal appeals disagreed. Defendant went to the victim's home seeking money in order to obtain drugs. When he was unable to obtain money, he raped the victim. Evidence of the rape included defendant's semen, identified by DNA correlation, on bed and bath linens from the victim's home. In order to keep the victim from reporting that he had raped her and stolen from her, he killed the victim by strangling her with an electrical cord. According to the State's proof, death by strangulation would take minutes, even if pressure were firm and constant. Defendant admitted, as well, that he took money from the victim. The proof demonstrated that defendant committed a willful, deliberate, malicious and premeditated killing of the victim. Additionally, defendant committed a killing in the perpetration of both a rape and a larceny. The DNA proof was thoroughly presented and tested at the trial. The jury had the opportunity to evaluate the credibility of the evidence and the witnesses with respect to the DNA evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Lee v. Dotson

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Hardeman County, Tennessee, denying his petition for writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of attempted first degree murder and aggravated assault. The trial court sentenced the inmate as a Range III, career offender, to sixty years. Furthermore, the inmate raised for the first time on appeal an issue concerning his career offender classification.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Muhammad v. State

DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of the decision of the Criminal Court for Hamilton County (Tennessee), which denied his petition for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of attempted second-degree murder, attempted voluntary manslaughter, and two counts of aggravated assault; he currently appealed from the denial of his petition for postconviction relief. The appellate court affirmed however, stating that it rejected his challenge to the constitutionality and imposition of consecutive sentencing, as both issues were raised and decided on direct appeal. Thus, they were previously determined under T.C.A. § 40-30-106(f) (2006). Appellate counsel was not ineffective for failing to raise a change of venue issue because the appellate court was unable to conclude that the issue would have been meritorious if raised on appeal.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Shabazz v. Worthington


No. E2008-01627-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 110



February 11, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Shabazz v. Worthington, 2009 Tenn. LEXIS 575 (Tenn., Aug. 31, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court is Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Morgan County. No. 9394. E. Eugene Eblen, Judge.
Shabazz v. Worthington, 2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 801 (Tenn. Crim. App., Oct. 15, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court is Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed a writ of habeas corpus. The Morgan County Circuit Court, Tennessee, summarily dismissed the petition. Petitioner appealed. The State filed a motion requesting that the appellate court affirm the habeas corpus court's denial of relief pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted petitioner of second degree murder and attempted second degree murder. He was sentenced to consecutive thirty and fifteen year sentences, respectively. He filed a petition for habeas corpus relief, arguing that Tennessee Code Annotated section 39-13-210, the second degree murder statute, was unconstitutional because it prohibited knowing killings perpetrated in self-defense. However, Tennessee case law did not support the claim. A killing in self-defense was considered justifiable under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-11-611(a). Furthermore, petitioner's complaint concerning the jury instruction on the mens rea of knowing did not meet the requirements for habeas corpus relief. Therefore, the habeas corpus court properly dismissed the petition for failure to state a claim warranting habeas corpus relief.


OUTCOME: The State's motion was granted, and the judgment of the habeas corpus court was affirmed.

January 28, 2008, Session 
February 5, 2009, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P.3; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part; Case Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for McMinn County. No. 00-115-117. Allen Wallace, Senior Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for McMinn County, Tennessee, that convicted him of premeditated first-degree murder, attempted premeditated first-degree murder, and aggravated arson under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-202(a)(1) and Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-14-302 (1999) and imposed a capital sentence, arguing that the evidence was insufficient to support his convictions.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court held that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction of premeditated first-degree murder, attempted premeditated first-degree murder, and aggravated arson where the evidence showed that (1) defendant began drinking heavily; (2) defendant became angered with his ex-wife, with whom he lived, when she refused to give him money to buy more beer; (3) defendant brandished a knife and ordered his ex-wife and the victim, an elderly man who shared a mobile home with defendant and defendant's ex-wife, to the front of the trailer and threatened to slit the victim's throat; (4) defendant grabbed his ex-wife when she tried to break away to call for help, pushed her down, and put the knife to her throat; (5) defendant retrieved duct tape and bound his ex-wife and the victim to prevent their escape while continuously telling them that they were going to die that night; (6) defendant retrieved a jug of kerosene that he poured throughout the trailer, slashing some on the victim and his ex-wife; (7) defendant unplugged all fire alarms and released his ex-wife's dog; and (8) defendant twisted a newspaper, ignited it, placed it next to the stove, and left.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence for the attempted first-degree murder conviction was reduced from 25 years in prison to the presumptive sentence of 20 years. In all other respects, including the imposition of the death sentence, the judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Boutchiche


No. E2007-00473-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 27


April 29, 2008, Session 
January 12, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Boutchiche, 2009 Tenn. LEXIS 314 (Tenn., June 22, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed as Modified. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Knox County. No. 80258. Richard R. Baumgartner, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed as Modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Criminal Court for Knox County (Tennessee) convicting him of sexual battery and sentencing him to two years in prison.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court held that the trial court did not err by denying defendant's motion for permission to question the victim regarding her testimony at the first trial that she told defendant that she was a lesbian because: (1) it was not admissible under Tenn. R. Evid. 412, as during the second trial the victim did not testify about her sexual orientation and the prosecutor made no reference to it; (2) it was inadmissible to impeach the victim's credibility under Tenn. R. Evid. 608 because the record did not support defendant's claim that the victim lied about her sexual orientation during the first trial; and (3) the evidence was inadmissible under Tenn. R. Evid. 616 because it was not relevant to any issue at trial. The trial court did not err by admitting a tape recording of the victim's 911 call as an excited utterance under Tenn. R. Evid. 803(2) because: (1) defendant conceded that the sexual battery was a startling event and that the victim's statement related to it; (2) the victim was 18 years old and had recently experienced a sexual assault; and (3) throughout the recording, the victim cried and experienced difficulty in speaking with the operator.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed; his sentence was modified to one year.

State v. Hilt

COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE

January 7, 2009, Filed

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Criminal Court for Hamilton County, Tennessee, that convicted him of felony murder under Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 39-15-401 and 39-15-402, arguing that the trial court erred in denying his motion to acquit.

OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

Code Ann. § 40-35-114 that were neither admitted by defendant nor determined by a jury beyond a reasonable doubt. This error resulted in a need for modification with regard to defendant's sentence for the aggravated robbery and aggravated burglary.

Draper v. State


No. E2007-01485-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 943


July 30, 2008, Assigned on Briefs 
December 5, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Draper v. State, 2009 Tenn. LEXIS 459 (Tenn., May 4, 2009)
Post-conviction relief denied at Draper v. State, 2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1072 (Tenn. Crim. App., Dec. 21, 2010)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Draper v. Lindamood, 2014 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 94 (Tenn. Crim. App., Jan. 31, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Sullivan County. No. C53,688. R. Jerry Beck, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal Court for Sullivan County, Tennessee, dismissed defendant's petition for post-conviction relief from his convictions for first degree murder and aggravated child abuse. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that he complied with the statute of limitations, T.C.A. § 40-30-102(a), that there was no statute of limitations for newly arising claims, and that the post-conviction statute of limitations was unconstitutional. The appellate court found that because there was no direct appeal of his convictions, defendant had one year from October 26, 2002, the date his judgments of conviction became final, to file his post-conviction claim. The present petition was filed over three and one-half years beyond that time. The evidence which defendant claimed was newly discovered was not of the type that was subject to the tolling provision. The Post-Conviction Procedure Act provided a one-year statute of limitations, and among those exceptions there was no provision for newly discovered evidence claims other than new scientific evidence, § 40-30-102(a), (b)(1)-(3). It was not appropriate for the appellate court to consider the allegations of the petition relative to coram nobis relief. Defendant's claims had not been heard on the merits, Tennessee Code Annotated section 40-30-106(h) (2006), but the petition was untimely. Defendant's other issues were waived.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Kouns


No. M2006-02788-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 870


November 14, 2007, Session 
November 5, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Trial Court is Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part; and Remanded. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Marion County. No. 7736, 7746 A-B, 7739, 7774, 7745 A-B-C, 7751. Thomas W. Graham, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Trial Court is Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part; and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were charged in the Circuit Court for Marion County (Tennessee) with the promotion of methamphetamine manufacture for purchasing an immediate methamphetamine precursor. The court dismissed the indictments. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in holding a post-indictment, pretrial hearing during which the trial court went on a fact-finding expedition. The court of appeals disagreed. The trial court dismissed the indictments based upon its determination that Tennessee Code Annotated section 39-17-433(a)(1) did not apply to the purchase of an immediate methamphetamine precursor due to the existence of Tennessee Code Annotated section 39-17-433(a)(2), which applied to the purchase of more than nine grams of immediate methamphetamine precursor. The trial court also determined that the State could not be allowed to amend the indictments to charge under subsection (a)(2) because the State could not prove that defendants purchased more than nine grams of immediate methamphetamine precursor in one purchase. Subsection (a)(1) applied to the purchase of nine grams or less of immediate methamphetamine precursor because the legislature did not intend to restrict punishment to those who purchased more than nine grams of precursor and absolve those who purchased nine grams or less of precursor with intent to manufacture methamphetamine.


OUTCOME: The trial court's dismissal of the indictments was reversed. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

State v. Flannel

COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 821


July 1, 2008, Assigned on Briefs 
October 13, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Flannel, 2009 Tenn. LEXIS 205 (Tenn., Mar. 23, 2009)
Post-conviction relief denied at Flannel v. State, 2012 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 592 (Tenn. Crim. App., Aug. 1, 2012)
Writ denied by Flannel v. State, 2014 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1133 (Tenn. Crim. App., Dec. 17, 2014)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Certificate of appealability denied Flannel v. Parris, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 135215 (W.D. Tenn., Sept. 30, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 03-07354. Carolyn Wade Blackett, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) of one count of murder in perpetration of a theft and one count of premeditated murder. He was sentenced to life imprisonment for both convictions, which were merged. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his premeditated murder conviction because the proof at trial showed that he did not intentionally kill the victim, but rather, he killed the victim in self-defense or under strong provocation due to the victim's unwelcome sexual advances toward him. The court of appeals disagreed. The proof established that defendant was upset because the victim made unwanted sexual advances toward him. The proof also established that defendant decided he wanted to rob the victim. At some point in the evening, defendant pretended to fall asleep and the victim went to his bedroom and fell asleep. Defendant took the victim's gun, woke the victim up, demanded money from him, and shot him multiple times in the face and head. The evidence further showed that defendant called his girlfriend from the victim's cell phone and bragged about his intent to kill the victim. Accordingly, a rational jury could have found beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant exercised reflection and judgment prior to killing the victim, and thus, the killing was intentional and premeditated.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

530 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. LePore


No. E2007-00893-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 806


January 30, 2008, Assigned on Briefs 
October 13, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court is Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Sevier County. No. 9392. O. Duane Slone, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court is Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury of the Sevier County Circuit Court (Tennessee) convicted defendant of violating Tennessee's former Sexual Offender Registration and Monitoring Act, and the trial court sentenced him to eleven months, twenty-nine days to be served as one hundred eighty days in confinement and the remainder on supervised probation. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that, at the time he was charged with violating the Act, the Act violated due process. The court agreed with the State that the Act did not violate due process by criminalizing behavior outside a registrant's control because former Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-39-104 (repealed 2004) did not require the registrant to mail the monitoring form. It required that a registrant "cause such form to be delivered" to the Tennessee Bureau of Investigation (TBI). Registrants could use any medium necessary to return the form as long as the form was delivered to the TBI no more than 10 days after the registrant received it. The trial court concluded that the Act was clear in that it required defendant actually to deliver the monitoring form to the TBI within 10 days. Defendant did not contest that ruling on appeal, and the court found no merit to his due process argument. A TBI records custodian testified in person about defendant's violation. Defendant did not explain how the Act had a discriminatory effect on him. Moreover, the Act did not violate equal protection, as it applied equally to all registrants. Defendant failed to allege discriminatory selective enforcement in his case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted for having marijuana on his person while in a jail cell following his arrest. 532 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Shields


No. W2007-01861-CCA-R9-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 795


March 4, 2008, Session 
October 7, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Shields, 2009 Tenn. LEXIS 536 (Tenn., Aug. 24, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 9 Interlocutory Appeal; Judgment of the Criminal Court is Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 07-00531. Paula Skahan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court is Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) denying his motion to dismiss the indictment charging him with possession of cocaine with intent to sell, possession of cocaine with intent to deliver, and driving on a suspended license.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court held that because the Tennessee drug tax under Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-4-2801 was not a criminal punishment for purposes of the double jeopardy clause under U.S. Const. amend. V and Tenn. Const. art. I, § 10, defendant's prosecution for possession of cocaine with intent to sell or deliver would not impose a second punishment for the same act. The drug tax was not a criminal punishment because: (1) the drug tax on its face revealed a clear legislative intent for the act to be a civil remedy; (2) taxes had not been historically regarded as punishment; (3) the imposition of the drug tax did not require a finding that the dealer had a particular mental state; (4) Tennessee's tax rate was not so high as to impose a criminal punishment; (5) although the tax was conditioned upon the commission of a crime, it was not restricted to persons who had been arrested as it contained provisions under Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 67-4-2805(a) by which a dealer could pay the tax voluntarily and anonymously; and (6) the tax expressly stated in Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-4-2801 that its purpose was to create revenue for use by law enforcement in addressing drug crimes and for the general fund.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

State v. Lucas


No. M2007-01411-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 752


February 20, 2008, Session 
September 26, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Lucas, 2009 Tenn. LEXIS 214 (Tenn., Mar. 16, 2009)
Post-conviction relief denied at Lucas v. State, 2012 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 312 (Tenn. Crim. App., May 9, 2012)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Lucas v. Westbrooks, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 187991 (M.D. Tenn., Oct. 16, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Williamson County. No. II-CR121536. Timothy L. Easter, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to rape of a child. The Circuit Court for Williamson County, Tennessee, sentenced him to twenty-five years, to be served at 100%, in the Tennessee Department of Correction. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: When defendant pled guilty to the rape of a child, he admitted that, while he and the victim were "playing doctor," he had touched the victim's vaginal area and forced her to perform fellatio on him. The trial court found two enhancing factors were applicable: (1) he had a previous history of criminal conduct, and (2) defendant abused a position of private trust. The Court of Criminal Appeals of Tennessee upheld the decision of the trial court sentencing him to twenty-five years. The trial court properly sentenced defendant pursuant to the amended provisions of Tennessee's Sentencing Act. There was sufficient proof to find that the crime occurred after the June 7, 2005 effective date of the amendments. The application of enhancement and mitigating factors did not violate the Sixth Amendment. The trial court considered all the requisite principles of sentencing prior to imposing the twenty-five-year sentence, and defendant failed to carry his burden of showing an improper sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

535 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Dick v. State


No. M2007-00542-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 735


May 13, 2008, Assigned on Briefs 
September 19, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Maury County. No. 13702. Jim T. Hamilton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner entered a best interests guilty plea in the Circuit Court for Maury County (Tennessee) to second degree murder in exchange for a sentence of twenty-three years. After his petition for postconviction relief was denied, petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner argued, inter alia, that his guilty pleas was not entered knowingly and voluntarily because counsel did not advise him of all the proof and possible defenses in his case. The court of appeals disagreed. At the post-conviction hearing, the petitioner claimed his plea was unknowing and involuntary because he was told to say "yes, sir" to the trial court's questions if he "didn't want 60 years in the penitentiary." As noted by the post-conviction court, the record established that the petitioner knowingly, intelligently, and voluntarily pleaded guilty to second degree murder and received a favorable twenty-three year sentence. During the plea, petitioner informed the trial court that counsel had thoroughly discussed the facts of the case with him, that he understood the strengths and weaknesses of his case, that he understood his rights not to plead guilty and go to trial, and that he was entering his plea "freely and voluntarily." Therefore, petitioner did not carry his burden of demonstrating that his plea was unknowing and involuntary.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

536 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Scott


No. M2006-02067-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 733


October 24, 2007, Session 
September 17, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part, Sentence Modified. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Cannon County. No. F05-02. Don Ash, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part, Sentence Modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Cannon County (Tennessee) of vehicular homicide by intoxication and three counts of vehicular assault. Defendant received an effective sentence of eight years. The sentence was ordered to be served by one year in confinement and sixteen years on probation. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the length of the probationary term was excessive. The court of appeals agreed. There was nothing in the record to support a finding that sixteen years of probation was the least severe measure necessary to achieve the purposes for which the sentence was imposed. The record reflected that defendant had discontinued the use of alcohol and drugs, regularly attended AA meetings, had a strong support system, had talked with others about drinking and driving, and had expressed her desire to continue to be a positive influence in keeping intoxicated drivers off the road. Defendant had no prior criminal record and was gainfully employed. The trial court ordered a year of confinement in addition to the maximum probationary term. The probation component of defendant's sentence should have been set at eight years. Therefore, the length of defendant's probationary term was improper. In addition, the trial court properly suspended defendant's driving privileges for eight years, although improperly terming it a "revocation."


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence for vehicular homicide was modified to be served with one year in jail followed by eight years of probation. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

State v. Moore


No. M2007-02515-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 732

September 16, 2008, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1]

DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Circuit Court Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part; Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Bedford County (Tennessee) of five counts of selling.5 grams or more of cocaine and was sentenced to 24 years. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court committed reversible error in consolidating the charge for the April 11 offense with the other four. The court of appeals agreed as to the April 11 conviction. The agent followed a confidential informant to a trailer park but did not see where she went inside the park and did not see her in the presence of defendant. Although the State placed into evidence the audio recordings of the informant's April 11 telephone call to defendant and her transactional meeting with him, the State relied upon the informant's testimony to identify defendant's voice on the tapes. Defendant testified that he not only sold no drugs to the informant but also that he never resided in the trailer park. Although the evidence of defendant's guilt of the offense was sufficient, it was not overwhelming, nor did it rise to the same level as that presented for the other offenses. The weaker nature of the proof of the offense lead to a conclusion that the jury's verdict was most likely unfairly influenced by proof of the other offenses. Therefore, the error was not harmless.


OUTCOME: One conviction was reversed and remanded for a new trial. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

Curry v. State


No. E2007-02526-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 604

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court is Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Johnson County. No. 5035. Robert E. Cupp, Judge.
State v. Curry, 2001 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 586 (Tenn. Crim. App., Aug. 2, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court is Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed the judgment of the Criminal Court for Johnson County, Tennessee, summarily dismissing his petition for writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted petitioner of three separate counts of aggravated rape. The trial court sentenced petitioner to three twenty-two-year sentences to be run consecutively to each other. Petitioner was unsuccessful on appeal. Petitioner filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus. The habeas corpus court summarily dismissed the petition, because petitioner did not adhere to the mandatory requirements for filing a petition for writ of habeas corpus which required him to attach a copy of his prior petition. He also failed to state a cognizable basis for habeas relief. Petitioner's first three issues attacking the validity of his indictments were without merit. The indictments set forth both the elements of the offense and the statute which defined the offense. Therefore, the indictments were sufficient to vest jurisdiction in the convicting court. His claims concerning the insufficiency of the evidence and erroneous jury instructions could not form the basis for habeas corpus relief. Any arguments concerning the application of a prior conviction to enhance his sentence were moot.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Grasty v. State


No. E2007-01386-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 602


June 24, 2008, Session 
August 1, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Morgan County. No. 9210. E. Eugene Eblen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After entering guilty pleas, appellant petitioner received a sentence of 17 years to be served at 100 percent for especially aggravated kidnapping and a sentence of 2 years to be served at 30 percent for escape, the sentences to be served consecutively. The Circuit Court for Morgan County, Tennessee, denied the petitioner's pro se petition for habeas corpus relief. The petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the petitioner contended the habeas corpus court erred by dismissing the petition without a full evidentiary hearing. The appellate court disagreed, finding that although the petitioner complained that he was erroneously ordered to serve 100 percent of his 17-year sentence, he failed to allege that his sentence was imposed in direct contravention of any statute. The 100 percent release eligibility date was required by operation of law under T.C.A. § 40-35-501(i)(2)(C) (1997), and was not, therefore, illegal. Similarly, the petitioner's claim that the consecutive sentencing was improper did not avail him of habeas corpus relief. The petitioner's claim, even if true, would have rendered the judgments voidable rather than void, and was not, therefore, a cognizable claim for habeas corpus relief. Moreover, the petitioner was sentenced three years before the decision in Blakely; his case was a separate collateral attack and was not in the pipeline.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

OVERVIEW: The inmates were each convicted of various crimes and they both received the death penalty for the murder of one of the victims. OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Thompson v. State


No. M2007-02035-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 595


June 18, 2008, Assigned on Briefs 
July 3, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Thompson v. State, 2008 Tenn. LEXIS 832 (Tenn., Oct. 27, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Bedford County. No. 10595. J. B. Cox, Judge.
State v. Thompson, 2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1137 (Tenn. Crim. App., Dec. 20, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Circuit Court for Bedford County (Tennessee) convicted petitioner inmate of 17 crimes involving his sexual contact with three minor girls. Those convictions were affirmed on direct appeal. The inmate filed a petition for post-conviction relief, alleging that he did not receive effective assistance of counsel under the Sixth Amendment and Tenn. Const. art. I, § 9. The post-conviction court denied the petition. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: Counsel did not specifically confront one of the victims with inconsistent statements concerning where she alleged the inmate touched her and concerning what she wore during the incident. Also, counsel's decision to refrain from harsh line-by-line cross-examination was within the discretion of defense counsel, particularly because of the age of the victims. However, counsel skillfully cross-examined two of the victims using their pre-trial statements. In addition, counsel met with the inmate a number of times, spoke with potential witnesses, and proceeded to trial based on the inmate's defense that he was innocent. Thus, counsel was adequately prepared for the trial. In addition, because the State and the victim presented no evidence at trial concerning the victim's sexual behavior, the credibility exception to Rule 412 did not apply, and a Rule 412 motion would not have been successful. Finally, the inmate's prior bad check convictions were properly admitted into evidence under Rule 609 for the purpose of impeachment. Thus, the inmate's ineffective assistance of counsel claims failed. Therefore, the post-conviction court properly denied his petition for relief.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the post-conviction court's judgment.

OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted for sexually assaulting the victim, a child, and later touching a second victim's right buttock. On appeal, the court held that the inmate was not denied his right to a fair trial on the ground that the trial court used the Coley case to exclude a defense expert's testimony that, concerning the reliability of eyewitness identification, certain leading questions could elicit certain answers, even though the Coley case was overruled by the Copeland case after the inmate filed his petition but before the hearing on the petition, because the rule in Copeland did not apply to the inmate on his collateral appeal. Chalmers v. State


No. W2006-00424-CCA-R3-PD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 464


September 11, 2007, Session 
June 25, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. P-24695. W. Fred Axley, Judge.
State v. Chalmers, 28 S.W.3d 913, 2000 Tenn. LEXIS 566 (Tenn., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed a judgment of the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) denying his petition for postconviction relief from his convictions of first-degree felony murder and especially aggravated robbery and death sentence.


OVERVIEW: The court held that counsel was not ineffective for failing to properly prepare mitigation evidence for sentencing, including witnesses' testimony that the inmate was a good, nice, and caring person, that his neighborhood was crime-ridden, and that he was placed in special education classes, because he failed to show that had the mitigating evidence been presented at trial, it was reasonably probable that the outcome of his sentencing would have been different. The witnesses were the inmate's family, friends, teachers, and coworkers and the mitigating evidence was subjected to substantial impeachment and potentially devastating rebuttal. Even if the inmate had a significant psychological disorder, the jury may have concluded that the mitigation evidence was insufficient to preclude imposition of the death penalty when weighed against the aggravating evidence. The inmate's claim that counsel failed to develop a comprehensive theory of defense was rejected because counsel testified that the theory was that the inmate was unable to form the intent to justify a first-degree murder charge based on his assertion that, due to his use of cocaine, he could not remember what had happened.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying the inmate's petition was affirmed.

June 24, 2008, Filed

Demonbreun v. Bell, 226 S.W.3d 321, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 452 (Tenn., 2007)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The petitioner inmate filed a petition for habeas corpus relief. The Criminal Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, denied the petition, and the inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: In 1997, a jury convicted the inmate of one count of second degree murder and one count of aggravated assault, and was sentenced to an effective sentence of twenty-five years in prison. The instant petition was the inmate's third petition for habeas corpus relief. The inmate argued that his conviction was void because the trial court never conducted a hearing on his motion for new trial and the issue was not previously litigated. The appellate court ruled that while it agreed that the specific issue of whether the trial court's failure to perform its duty as a thirteenth juror entitled the inmate to habeas corpus relief was not previously litigated, any failure by the trial court in this regard did not afford him the relief he sought. Failure of the trial court to exercise its role as thirteenth juror would make the conviction voidable. Also, the inmate argued that the trial court lacked the statutory authority to enter the judgments against him. The appellate court ruled that the inmate's judgment was not void on its face and he was not entitled to habeas corpus relief.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Looper v. State


No. E2005-01918-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 430


March 26, 2008, Assigned on Briefs 
June 2, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Cumberland County. No. 5346. J.S. Daniel, Judge.
State v. Looper, 118 S.W.3d 386, 2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 83 (Tenn. Crim. App., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Cumberland County (Tennessee), which denied his petition for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The inmate had been convicted of murder and currently appealed the denial of his petition for postconviction relief; the appellate court affirmed. The basic problem with the inmate's claims was that, even though it was his burden to do so under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-110(f) (2006), he presented virtually no relevant proof at the evidentiary hearing. Rather, he relied on detailed and lengthy prehearing pleadings and appellate briefs, which could not substitute for proof. Further, he failed to show that he received the ineffective assistance of counsel under U.S. Const. Amend. VI; Tenn. Const. Art. I, § 9. Although the inmate elicited testimony from the victim's widow and daughter that trial counsel did not contact them, the inmate did not show that either witness would have provided information helpful or even material to his defense. In fact, the victim's widow testified that she was unsure whether she would have spoken to trial counsel, and the victim's daughter unequivocally stated that she would not have done so.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Simmons v. State

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Hardeman County, Tennessee, denying his writ of habeas corpus.

Ritchie v. Carlton


No. E2007-01606-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 383


January 30, 2008, Assigned on Briefs 
May 14, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Habeas corpus proceeding at, Petition dismissed by State v. Hamilton, 2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 383 (Tenn. Crim. App., May 25, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Johnson County. No. 5093. Lynn W. Brown, Judge.
Ritchie v. State, 2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 708 (Tenn. Crim. App., Aug. 18, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed the judgment of the Johnson County Criminal Court, Tennessee, summarily dismissing his petition for writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of aggravated rape and armed robbery. The trial court imposed a life sentence. Petitioner filed a habeas corpus petition, alleging that his judgments were void because the judge did not sign them, that his life sentence was void because the aggravated rape statute was unconstitutionally vague, and that his indictment was constructively amended by the jury instructions. The habeas court summarily dismissed the petition. Petitioner's claim concerning his indictment was not presented on appeal. The Court of Criminal Appeals of Tennessee found that petitioner's sentence had not expired, and the convicting court had jurisdiction over petitioner, the actus reus, and the subject matter. Petitoner's claim that the trial judge did not sign the judgment of conviction did not render the judgment void. Petitioner's claim that his life sentence was void because the aggravated rape statute was unconstitutionally vague was not cognizable in a habeas proceeding. Accordingly, the habeas court did not err by dismissing the petition without a hearing.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Perry


No. M2007-00903-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 317


January 8, 2008, Assigned on Briefs 
April 28, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief dismissed at La Sean Perry v. State, 2013 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 926 (Tenn. Crim. App., Oct. 24, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Maury County. No. 13103. Robert Holloway, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by jury, before the Circuit Court for Maury County, Tennessee, of second degree murder. Defendant appealed the conviction.


OVERVIEW: The victim's cousin saw the victim driving fast, and he saw gunshot from another car. Subsequently, defendant to a pat-down search by police during a traffic stop. A handgun was found. On appeal, defendant presented the following issues for review: (1) whether the trial court erred in denying defendant's motion to suppress, pursuant to U.S. Const. amend. IV and Tenn. Const. art. I, § 7; and (2), whether the trial court erred in failing to find any mitigating factors when imposing the sentence. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the defendant's motion to suppress because defendant consented to the search. Moreover, the officer conducting the search at the time of the traffic stop had reason to believe defendant might have been armed or dangerous. The officer was justified in conducting a limited pat-down search. As to the sentence, defendant was subjected to range of 15 to 25 years, pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-112(a)(1). When sentencing defendant to 25 years, the trial court properly applied enhancement factors. The trial court also considered, before rejecting, two mitigating factors pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. 40-35-113(6), (12).


OUTCOME: For the reasons stated herein, the judgment of the trial court is affirmed.

State v. Owen


No. M2007-02069-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 343


April 22, 2008, Assigned on Briefs 
April 24, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Owen, 2008 Tenn. LEXIS 630 (Tenn., Aug. 25, 2008)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Owen v. State, 2013 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 127 (Tenn. Crim. App., Feb. 13, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Hickman County. No. 05-5132CR. Robert E. Lee Davies, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the Circuit Court for Hickman County (Tennessee), defendant pleaded guilty to two counts of rape of a child, leaving the sentence to be determined by the trial court. The trial court sentenced defendant to consecutive eighteen-year sentences. Defendant appealed the judgments, claiming the trial court's decision to order consecutive sentences violated established Sixth Amendment precedent.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the trial court's decision to order consecutive sentences pursuant to Tennessee Code Annotated section 40-35-115(b)(5) as violating his Sixth Amendment rights to trial by jury. Defendant argued that the Blakely rule, under which fact-finding by a judge violated a defendant's right to a jury trial if the fact-finding subjected the defendant to increased punishment that would not have been allowed but for the fact-finding, should apply not only to sentencing enhancement factors, but also to the determination of whether multiple sentences should be served concurrently or consecutively. However, the appellate court noted that Tennessee courts had consistently held that the consecutive sentencing scheme did not violate the Sixth Amendment. Having reviewed the record, the appellate court concluded that the trial court did not err in ordering defendant's sentences to be served consecutively, and that for purposes of T.C.A. §40-35-102(1), the length of defendant's sentences were justly deserved in relation to the seriousness of the offenses and were no greater than that deserved for the offenses committed.


OUTCOME: The judgments of the trial court were affirmed.

State v. Swofford


No. W2007-00448-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 268


November 6, 2007, Session 
April 7, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 06-08856. James C. Beasley, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant entered a plea of guilty to one count of driving under the influence (DUI), first offense, the Criminal Court for Shelby County, Tennessee, sentenced him to 11 months, 29 days, to be suspended after serving 48 hours in confinement. As a condition of his guilty plea, defendant properly reserved a certified question of law as to whether he was subjected to an unconstitutional traffic stop.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended his motion to suppress should have been granted because the officer did not have specific and articulable facts to believe that an offense had been committed. Specifically, defendant argued that the officer did not ascertain that the substance which defendant threw out of his car was in fact a cigarette package until after the traffic stop was initiated when defendant confirmed that he had thrown a cigarette package onto the surface of the parking lot. The appellate court disagreed, finding that whether the item was a cigarette package, a piece of paper, or some other type of garbage or other waste material, the officer's observations provided reasonable suspicion that defendant had violated the littering statute. As such, the officer had reasonable suspicion supported by specific and articulable facts to conduct an investigatory stop, and the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

555 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Byrd


No. E2006-02619-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 254


September 25, 2007, Session 
April 2, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Hamilton County. No. 257167 Rebecca Stern, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of attempted first degree premeditated murder, a Class A felony, and aggravated assault, a Class C felony. The Criminal Court for Hamilton County, Tennessee, merged the offenses and sentenced defendant to life without the possibility of parole as a repeat violent offender. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant stabbed his father's girlfriend. The victim was unarmed. Defendant walked into the kitchen to obtain a knife, held the knife behind him while he approached the unaware victim, and told her "I'll teach you" just before stabbing her. Although there was evidence that defendant may have been arguing with his father before he stabbed the victim, she testified that she and defendant were getting along well that day. The evidence was sufficient for the jury to infer that defendant formed the intent to kill the victim prior to his stabbing her and that he committed the act with premeditation. The trial court's decision to sentence defendant under the repeat violent offenders statute did not violate his rights to due process and equal protection of the law. The legislature's decision to impose the very severe sentence of life imprisonment without possibility of parole upon those criminals who repeatedly commit violent offenses was rationally related to its desire to protect the public and deter crime.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Lowe v. State


No. E2006-02028-CCA-MR3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 176


August 21, 2007, Assigned on Briefs 
March 10, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Lowe v. State, 2008 Tenn. LEXIS 610 (Tenn., Aug. 25, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Blount County. No. C-14586 D. Kelly Thomas, Jr., Judge.
State v. Lowe, 2002 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 783 (Tenn. Crim. App., Sept. 16, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was convicted in the Circuit Court for Blount County (Tennessee) of two counts of first degree murder and one count of especially aggravated robbery, and he was sentenced to two concurrent life sentences without the possibility of parole. After his motion for postconviction relief was denied, petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner argued, inter alia, that counsel was ineffective for failing to test bloody shorts worn by a witness. The court of appeals disagreed. Petitioner did not prove that he suffered prejudice as a result of the shorts not being tested. Counsel's explanation of why he chose not to request the shorts be tested left something to be desired, especially considering that counsel would not have necessarily been required to reveal whose blood was on the shorts. Petitioner was required, however, to show that he was prejudiced by failure of counsel to have the shorts tested. As it was not known whose blood was on the shorts, it was unknown as to what effect at trial the bloody shorts evidence might have had. Although petitioner was not given funds to test the shorts at the post-conviction stage, he could have questioned the witness at the post-conviction hearing as to whose blood was on the shorts. Petitioner had not proven that there was a reasonable probability that, but for counsel's unprofessional errors, the result of the proceeding would have been different.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

557 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Taylor


No. M2005-01941-CCA-R3-DD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 200



March 7, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed and Case Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Williamson County. No. S-83428. Russ Heldman, Judge.
Taylor v. State, 1999 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 732 (Tenn. Crim. App., July 21, 1999)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed and Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Williamson County (Tennessee) of one count of first degree murder, and he was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred when it allowed defendant to waive his right to counsel because the colloquy between the trial court and defendant was insufficient to meet constitutional requirements. The court of appeals agreed. Specifically, defendant claimed that, although the trial court asked the routine questions required, his responses should have prompted further examination by the trial court, which was not done. The trial court allowed defendant to refuse to answer questions from his own counsel who was attempting to present an argument for defendant. Notably, defense counsel had not yet been discharged when the trial court refused to allow counsel to question defendant. Because defendant was still represented by counsel, counsel had a duty to zealously represent defendant. In the view of counsel, defendant would be better served if he were not allowed to represent himself. Counsel was not permitted to call witnesses or present evidence on behalf of defendant. The responses to counsel's questions were part of the inquiry that the situation demanded and the trial court did not "investigate as long and as thoroughly as the circumstances demanded."


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial.

State v. Bass


No. M2006-02563-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 185


October 23, 2007, Session 
February 28, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Bass, 2008 Tenn. LEXIS 769 (Tenn., Oct. 6, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Williamson County. No. II-CR04204. Timothy L. Easter, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Williamson County (Tennessee) of criminal simulation with a value of less than $ 1,000, theft of property greater than $ 1,000 but less than $ 10,000, tampering with the evidence, and forgery. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by not suppressing her statements to authorities because she was in custody at the time she made those statements and had not been given Miranda warnings. The court of appeals disagreed. The evidence did not preponderate against the trial court's finding that defendant was not in custody at the time she made statements to police officers. Detectives went to defendant's home, knocked, identified themselves and asked to speak with defendant. She was not arrested. Defendant invited the detectives into her home to speak with them. After asking a few questions, defendant indicated her intent to make things "as difficult as possible," and refused consent for a search of her computer. However, defendant was free to come and go as she pleased. At one point defendant left and went and picked her daughter up at school. There was no indication that the questioning of defendant took place in a context where her freedom to depart was restricted in any way. Therefore, defendant was not entitled to relief on that issue.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Bowen v. Carlton


No. E2007-01845-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 98


November 27, 2007, Assigned on Briefs 
February 20, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Bowen v. Carlton, 2008 Tenn. LEXIS 359 (Tenn., May 5, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Johnson County. No. 5085.Lynn W. Brown, Judge.
Bowen v. State, 1992 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 326 (Tenn. Crim. App., Apr. 10, 1992)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed the judgment of the Criminal Court for Johnson County, Tennessee, dismissing his habeas corpus petition.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of several counts of aggravated kidnapping, aggravated rape, and aggravated assault. He received an effective sentence of 145 years. In a habeas proceeding, petitioner argued that the trial court erred in failing to properly determine his indigency. The record on appeal did not include the activity in his inmate trust fund account, his motion to proceed in forma pauperis, or the pauper's oath and affirmation. Therefore, the appellate court could not review the matter. Summary dismissal of the habeas petition was proper because it did not state a cognizable claim for habeas corpus relief. Petitioner's claim that his indictments and his two convictions for aggravated assault were multiplicitous with two of his aggravated kidnapping convictions required the court to look beyond the face of the judgments; therefore, it was not a cognizable claim for habeas corpus relief. Petitioner's Blakely claim regarding his sentence would render the conviction voidable and not void; thus it was non-cognizable in habeas corpus review.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

560 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Thompson


No. W2007-00976-CCA-R9-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 79


December 4, 2007, Assigned on Briefs 
February 13, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 9 Interlocutory Appeal; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part, and Remanded. Interlocutory Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. Nos. 04-05231 & 04-05232. James C. Beasley, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part, and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal Court for Shelby County, Tennessee, convicted defendant, pursuant to a guilty plea, of contempt. The trial court dismissed the two charges of impersonation of a licensed professional on double jeopardy grounds but refused to dismiss the two theft charges. The State and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in refusing to dismiss the theft charges. The appellate court concluded that the elements of contempt were wholly different from the elements of both theft and impersonation of a licensed professional. The underlying facts supported all the charges. The evidence used to prove the charges against two individuals would be a part of but would not make up the entirety of the evidence used to prosecute the contempt charges. The contempt proceedings were not only based on defendant's pretending to be an attorney against the two individuals, but they were also based on similar acts against two others. The charges were not based on totally discrete acts, but partially discrete acts. The fact that the offenses addressed partially discrete acts and different victims suggested that separate prosecutions would not violate double jeopardy principles under the Tennessee Constitution. Three of the four factors supported allowing separate prosecution.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed denying dismissal of the theft charges; the judgment was reversed dismissing the charges of impersonation of a licensed professional.

 

561 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Harris


No. M2006-01532-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


280 S.W.3d 832; 2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 112


July 17, 2007, Assigned on Briefs 
February 6, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Harris, 2008 Tenn. LEXIS 629 (Tenn., Aug. 25, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed; Remanded. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Lawrence County. No. 25348. Jim T. Hamilton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed; Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant's motion to suppress evidence was denied, defendant pleaded guilty in the Circuit Court for Lawrence County (Tennessee) to possession of cocaine with intent to sell. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the search of his person pursuant to the vehicle exception was improper. The court of appeals agreed. The detention during the process of issuing the citations was not unduly protracted to accommodate the dog's sweep. Thus, the officer's actions were within constitutional bounds when he discovered information via the trained dog's reaction that the vehicle contained narcotics. However, when the dog reacted to the passenger side door and the officer asked defendant, the driver, why the dog would have reacted, defendant denied knowledge of contraband. The officer then conducted a "more thorough" pat-down of defendant. An extension of the vehicle search exception was inapt for two reasons. First, defendant left the vehicle before the police acquired any indication that the vehicle contained material that they would be entitled to seize; the dog apparently did not react to any substances secluded on defendant's person. Second, a passenger in the vehicle occupied the seat near the door where the dog reacted. Therefore, the officer's ultimate, warrantless search of defendant was not justified by constitutional principles governing vehicle searches.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded.

 

562 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mantey


No. E2006-00143-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 44


September 26, 2007, Assigned on Briefs 
January 29, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Mantey, 2008 Tenn. LEXIS 602 (Tenn., Aug. 25, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Washington County. No. 29580. Lynn W. Brown, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal Court for Washington County (Tennessee) of the sale of more than.5 grams of cocaine and sentenced as a Range I offender to 12 years. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by admitting a tape recording of the drug transaction into evidence and permitting it to be played for the jury because it was not properly authenticated and because it contained inadmissible hearsay. The court of appeals agreed, but found that any error was harmless. Although the informant identified defendant as the person that sold him the cocaine, he did not actually identify defendant's voice on the tape recording of the transaction. In consequence, the State failed to "tie together" the evidence as promised. Accordingly, the evidence should not have been admitted. Although the tape recording should not have been admitted into evidence absent an identification of defendant's voice, reversal was not required. The informant did not identify defendant's voice on the tape, but he did identify defendant as the person that sold him.9 grams of crack cocaine. In addition, the $ 200 in marked currency that had been provided to the informant to purchase the cocaine was found only hours later in defendant's front pocket. Under those circumstances, the erroneous admission of the tape recording was harmless error.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Aaron v. State


No. M2006-01983-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 74


August 15, 2007, Session 
January 22, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Aaron v. State, 2008 Tenn. LEXIS 465 (Tenn., June 23, 2008)

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 99-D-2360. Walter C. Kurtz, Judge.
State v. Aaron, 2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1123 (Tenn. Crim. App., Dec. 13, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, an inmate, sought review of the decision of the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), which denied his petition for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of especially aggravated sexual exploitation of a minor and false imprisonment and he currently appealed from the denial of his petition for postconviction relief. The appellate court affirmed however, stating that the sufficiency of the convicting evidence was not cognizable in a postconviction proceeding. Thus, his assignment of error was without merit. His counsel was not ineffective under U.S. Const. amend. VI or Tenn. Const, art. I, § 9 for not challenging the as-applied constitutionality of Tennessee Code Annotated section 39-17-1005. The statute's primary purpose was the protection of children and the inmate placed great reliance on the fact that the photographs at issue were never found and never seen by the jury. But, what the statute prohibited was not only the production of material involving lascivious exhibition, but the performance, which included a minor engaging in lascivious activities. The record also supported the determination that the inmate knowingly, voluntarily, and intelligently waived his right to testify under U.S. Const. amends. V, XIV and Tenn. Const, art. I, § 9.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
