State v. Tallant


No. E2006-02273-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 21


October 30, 2007, Session 
January 14, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Tallant, 2008 Tenn. LEXIS 449 (Tenn., June 30, 2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at Tallant v. State, 2014 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 692 (Tenn. Crim. App., July 15, 2014)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion denied by Tallant v. Perry, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 60788 (E.D. Tenn., May 9, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed in Part; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Knox County. No. 76020. Richard R. Baumgartner, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed in Part; Case Remanded


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal Court for Knox County (Tennessee) of two counts of first degree felony murder, one count of second degree murder, and two counts of aggravated child abuse. The trial court dismissed the second degree murder charge, merged the two felony murder convictions, and sentenced defendant to life in prison plus twenty-five years. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his convictions. The court of appeals disagreed. While neither of the medical professionals could testify as to who inflicted the injuries, defendant's wife testified that defendant was the child's primary caregiver, taking care of the child approximately eighty-five percent of the time. She testified to numerous questionable parenting practices on defendant's part. Both the wife and investigating police officers testified that the night the victim died, the victim's mother was frantic about the baby's well-being, while defendant appeared aloof and unconcerned. That evidence, though largely circumstantial, was sufficient for the jury to find beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant abused and neglected the victim in such a manner that led to serious bodily injury and ultimately death. The testimony that defendant was the primary caretaker and the medical examiner's testimony that the injuries could not have been accidentally inflicted were particularly significant and could have led the jury to reasonably conclude that the evidence excluded all reasonable hypotheses except for the guilt of defendant.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded to the trial court for merger of defendant's two aggravated child abuse convictions and a determination of whether consecutive sentences were appropriate. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

 

565 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Russell v. Bell


No. M2007-01298-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 66


November 14, 2007, Assigned on Briefs 
January 11, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Russell v. Bell, 2008 Tenn. LEXIS 485 (Tenn., June 2, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 87-F-2309. J. Randall Wyatt, Jr., Judge.
State v. Russell, 1990 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 36 (Tenn. Crim. App., Jan. 19, 1990)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of an order from the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), which granted the State's motion to dismiss his application for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of one count of first-degree burglary, one count of aggravated sexual battery, two counts of aggravated rape of one victim, and 12 counts of aggravated rape of another victim. He received a total effective sentence of 147 years and six months in prison. Petitioner filed an application for a writ of habeas corpus claiming that the sentences imposed by the trial court were unconstitutional because they were not set by a jury and were rendered void pursuant to the rule of law announced in Blakely. The trial court granted the State's motion to dismiss the petition. On appeal, the court found that petitioner's claim failed because even if a Blakely violation occurred, the violation would render the judgment voidable, not void. Petitioner's sentences were within the applicable range of punishment under the 1982 Sentencing Reform Act, Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 39-2-603, -606, -3-401 (1982). Petitioner's judgments of conviction were not void. The sentence of confinement had not expired. Accordingly, petitioner was not entitled to relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

566 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lynch


No. M2006-02158-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 57


October 24, 2007, Assigned on Briefs 
January 9, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Lynch, 2008 Tenn. LEXIS 351 (Tenn., Apr. 28, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Marshall County. No. 17142. Robert Crigler, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate pled guilty to violating the Tennessee Habitual Motor Vehicle Offender Act. The Circuit Court for Marshall County (Tennessee) sentenced him to three years in confinement. The inmate filed a petition for post-conviction relief, which the post-conviction court denied. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court did not see how the inmate was prejudiced by his attorneys' failure to call certain witnesses on his behalf. The inmate did not prove that the testimony addressing his sobriety and ability to work outweighed his more than 20 prior convictions. Additionally, the inmate's attorneys were not ineffective for not presenting witnesses because the inmate did not provide witness information to his attorneys. Furthermore, the appellate court concluded that the inmate voluntarily and intelligently pled guilty because, after being questioned by the post-conviction court at length pursuant to Tennessee Criminal Procedure Rule 11, the inmate stated that he understood that he was waiving his right to a jury trial and the right to appeal. Finally, although the post-conviction court erred by stating or believing that a habitual vehicle offender could not receive an alternative sentence, the error was harmless given the inmate's lengthy criminal record, which was an enhancement factor. Thus, under Sixth Amendment to the United States Constitution and article I, section 9, of the Tennessee Constitution, the inmate's ineffective assistance of counsel claim failed.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the post-conviction court's judgment.

State v. Morgan


No. E2006-00820-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


271 S.W.3d 217; 2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 3


April 24, 2007, Session 
January 7, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court are Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part and Remanded. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Knox County. No. 79909A. Mary Beth Leibowitz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Criminal Court for Knox County, Tennessee, convicting him for first degree murder by a destructive device.


OVERVIEW: Defendant threw a rock from an interstate overpass. This incident resulted in the death of a passenger in a vehicle traveling under the overpass. A jury convicted defendant of first degree murder by a destructive device. The trial court merged defendant's conviction for reckless homicide into the conviction for first degree murder by destructive device. The appellate court found the evidence insufficient to support defendant's conviction for first degree murder under T.C.A. § 39-13-202(a)(3). The trial court's jury instruction that the term "destructive device" could mean "anything" adapted for destruction, or "anything" capable of causing destruction was erroneous. A rock thrown from a highway overpass was not a "device" for purposes of T.C.A. § 39-13-202(a)(3). The appellate court reinstated the reckless homicide conviction and ordered defendant to serve the four-year sentence imposed for that offense.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment regarding defendant's conviction for first degree murder based upon the use of a destructive device and affirmed the remaining judgments. The judgment of conviction for reckless homicide was reinstated.

DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Robertson County (Tennessee), which denied his petition for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of selling less than 0.5 grams of cocaine. After a sentencing hearing, the trial court found that he was a career offender and sentenced him to the only available sentence, 15 years in prison, with a release eligibility of 60 percent. The trial court denied his petition for postconviction relief. On appeal, petitioner claimed that trial counsel was ineffective for failing to anticipate or raise a challenge to the enhancement of his sentence as unconstitutional pursuant to Blakely. The court found that Blakely did not apply to the facts of the case because the career offender statute found by the trial court was the result of prior convictions. The trial court did not enhance petitioner's sentence based upon a finding of facts that had to be found by a jury. The trial court had no discretion but to impose the only sentence provided for by law, 15 years.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Carruthers v. State


No. W2006-00376-CCA-R3-PD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 944


June 5, 2007, Session 
December 12, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Carruthers v. State, 2008 Tenn. LEXIS 411 (Tenn., May 27, 2008)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Carruthers v. Worthington, 2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 427 (Tenn. Crim. App., June 2, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. P-25948. Walter C. Kurtz, Judge, Sitting by Designation.
State v. Carruthers, 35 S.W.3d 516, 2000 Tenn. LEXIS 683 (Tenn., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was convicted in the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) of three counts of first degree murder and was sentenced to death. After his request for postconviction relief was denied, petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner argued, inter alia, that his various pretrial counsel collectively rendered ineffective assistance in that their failure to conduct any meaningful factual investigation led directly to his "disastrous" and compelled self-representation. The court of criminal appeals disagreed. Counsel filed numerous pretrial motions on petitioner's behalf, including motions for discovery, for a mental examination, to exclude evidence, for impeachment evidence, and for a notice of an alibi defense. Counsel estimated that he met with petitioner at least a dozen times during the six months of his representation and confirmed that his billing records reflected he had spent approximately 60.15 hours on the case. Petitioner's compelled self-representation resulted from his own misbehavior and nothing else. All of the counsel appointed to represent petitioner were competent and experienced trial attorneys who took the appropriate steps in their preparation of the case at the time they were relieved from representation. Moreover, petitioner did not produce any witnesses or evidence that pretrial counsel failed to investigate or uncover that would have altered the outcome of the trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Jones

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) of two counts of aggravated rape, which were merged. Defendant was sentenced to twenty-two years. Defendant appealed.

OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Kiser


No. E2005-02406-CCA-R3-DD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 890


April 24, 2007, Session 
November 29, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by, Remanded by State v. Kiser, 2009 Tenn. LEXIS 303 (Tenn., May 13, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court are Affirmed and the Case is Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Hamilton County. No. 238279. Stephen M. Bevil, Judge.
State v. Kiser, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 85 (Tenn., Jan. 31, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court are Affirmed and the Case is Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal Court for Hamilton County (Tennessee) of first degree premeditated murder and two counts of first degree felony murder. Defendant was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction for first degree premeditated murder. The court of criminal appeals disagreed. The proof at trial showed that defendant took his high-powered assault rifle with him to his friend's house. After his friend went to bed, defendant drove the friend's maroon pickup to a fruit stand. There, he tried to set the stand on fire. When the victim, a police officer, arrived in the parking lot, defendant hid behind the pickup and shot the victim as the victim approached. The evidence established that defendant shot the victim multiple times. Ballistics testing showed that the bullets recovered from the victim's body were fired from defendant's rifle. Defendant removed the victim's revolver and part of his bulletproof vest and returned to the friend's house, where he displayed the items and described the killing to his friend. Defendant had told witnesses of his animosity toward the police, demonstrating that he had a motive to kill the victim. Based on that evidence, the jury could reasonably and legitimately have concluded that defendant committed first degree premeditated murder.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded to the trial court in order for it to enter one judgment reflecting the merger of the three counts. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

Lewis v. State


No. M2007-01616-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 974



November 14, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Trial Court is Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Wayne County. No. 14165. Robert Holloway, Judge.
Lewis v. State, 2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 323 (Tenn. Crim. App., Apr. 20, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Trial Court is Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner applicant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Wayne County, Tennessee, dismissing his petition for habeas corpus relief. The State filed a motion to affirm under Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals.


OVERVIEW: The applicant was convicted of first degree premeditated murder, first degree felony murder and attempted robbery. The murder convictions merged into one conviction for first degree murder. The applicant alleged that the prosecutor's closing argument illegally amended the indictment, that count three of the indictment was constructively amended because the jury was allowed to convict him on a factual basis that effectively modified an element of the charged offense, and that the indictment for robbery did not cite a statute. The appellate court ruled that the trial court was correct in dismissing the petition for habeas corpus relief without a hearing and without appointment of counsel. The judgments attached to the petition for habeas corpus relief were facially valid. Also, even if the closing argument somehow resulted in an impermissible amendment of the indictment, the result would have made the applicant's judgment voidable rather than void. Furthermore, the indictment was sufficient to place the applicant on notice of the nature of the charge, confer jurisdiction upon the trial court, and protect against double jeopardy.


OUTCOME: The State's motion was granted, and the judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Meeks v. Bell


No. M2005-00626-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 962



November 13, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Meeks v. Bell, 2008 Tenn. LEXIS 215 (Tenn., Apr. 7, 2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Meeks v. Bell, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 444 (U.S., Jan. 12, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 04C-3157. Thomas W. Brothers, Judge.
Meeks v. Bell, 127 S. Ct. 1243, 167 L. Ed. 2d 60, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 1991 (U.S., 2007)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought a writ of habeas corpus, attacking his convictions for aggravate kidnapping, especially aggravated robbery, especially aggravated burglary, and extortion. On remand from the United States Supreme Court, the Circuit Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) dismissed the petition. The inmate challenged the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued that his sentences had expired because he had served more time in custody that the jury verdicts alone would have allowed. The inmate's sentences for aggravated kidnapping and extortion did not violate the Sixth Amendment because those sentences were the presumptive minimum sentences. The claim that the sentences imposed on the aggravated robbery and aggravated burglary convictions violated the Apprendi rule failed as that case law was not given retroactive application in cases such as the inmate's, which were collateral attacks upon final judgments of conviction. Moreover, the Apprendi rule and its progeny did not affect the trial court's ability to find facts essential to justify consecutive sentencing. Finally, nothing in federal case law expanded the inmate's right's under Tennessee's habeas corpus procedure to attack a judgment that was merely voidable on its face. Thus, the inmate's claims were not cognizable in a state habeas corpus proceeding.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing the petition for writ of habeas corpus was affirmed.

DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part, Case Remanded for Resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Criminal Court for Sumner County (Tennessee) convicting and sentencing him for rape of a child, incest, aggravated sexual battery, and two counts of especially aggravated sexual exploitation of a minor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for sexually assaulting the victim, his 14-year-old daughter. On appeal, the court held that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's convictions because the jury accredited the victim's testimony, which included her descriptions of defendant's physical assaults, as well as her identification of herself and defendant in a photograph depicting intercourse. The case was remanded for resentencing because of irregularities in the process.

Brown v. Parker


No. W2007-01122-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 775



October 3, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Brown v. Parker, 2008 Tenn. LEXIS 151 (Tenn., Mar. 3, 2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Brown v. Parker, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 7036 (U.S., Oct. 6, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Lauderdale County. No. 6133. Joe H. Walker, III, Judge.
State v. Brown, 2000 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 214 (Tenn. Crim. App., Mar. 9, 2000)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Tennessee criminal court found petitioner guilty of attempt to commit first degree murder and attempt to commit second degree murder, and his convictions and sentences were affirmed on direct appeal. Petitioner ultimately filed an application for writ of habeas corpus relief in the Circuit Court for Lauderdale County (Tennessee), which denied relief. Petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner sought habeas corpus relief under Tenn. Const. art. I, § 15 by alleging that his sentences were unconstitutional because they were not imposed by a jury and were thus rendered illegal pursuant to a new rule of law announced in the United States Supreme Court decision of Blakely v. Washington. However, the appellate court concluded that petitioner's Blakely claim failed because: (1) habeas corpus relief could be granted only if the petition established that the challenged judgment was void; and (2) even if a Blakely violation had occurred, the violation would have rendered petitioner's judgment merely voidable, not void. Thus, petitioner was not entitled to habeas corpus relief because he had established neither that his effective sentence had expired nor that the sentencing court was without jurisdiction or authority to enter the sentences imposed. Also, the appellate court held that Blakely v. Washington failed to afford petitioner a ground for postconviction relief under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-103 because the Blakely decision was not to be given retroactive application.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

Williams v. State


No. W2006-00875-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 769

September 27, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Williams v. Johnson, 2016 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 636 (Tenn. Crim. App., Aug. 26, 2016)

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. P-07638. Paula Skahan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate challenged a decision from the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee), which summarily dismissed his request for habeas corpus relief.


OVERVIEW: In 1973 and 1974, the inmate was sentenced to prison for various crimes, including three determinate life sentences for one count of armed robbery with a deadly weapon and two counts of murder during the perpetration of a robbery. The inmate's second petition for habeas corpus was dismissed, and this appeal followed. In affirming, the appellate court held that the inmate's sentences in this case were not void merely because the sentencing scheme under 1919 Tenn. Pub. Acts ch. 5, § 1 had been declared unconstitutional. The jury-imposed sentences were lawful when they were received. Post-conviction relief would have been untimely in this case because all similarly situated persons had until July 1, 1989, to file such a claim for relief. The inmate's claim that his Fourth, Fifth, Sixth, and Fourteenth Amendment rights were violated was meritless because he was not sentenced under the 1974 sentencing statutes. Next, the fact that some of the inmate's claims were unintelligible was not a sufficient reason to appoint counsel. Finally, an argument regarding the integrity of the indictments was waived.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

State v. McCobb


No. W2006-01517-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 772


April 10, 2007, Assigned on Briefs 
September 26, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed as Modified. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 04-08452. Paula Skahan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed as Modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal Court for Shelby County, Tennessee, convicted defendants of aggravated robbery, a Class B felony, and sentenced them as Range I, standard offenders to ten years in the Department of Correction. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants argued that the evidence was insufficient to support their convictions and the trial court erred in imposing ten-year sentences. The appellate court found that the victim testified that one defendant stalled him at the door before the other hit him with great force in the back of the head with a metal baseball bat and that when he fell down, one defendant stood over him with the bat raised demanding money. Defendants admitted that they robbed the victim and took money and pizzas from him. Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-114(7) did not apply because the victim did not suffer particularly great personal injury. Factor (5) applied as the victim was particularly vulnerable because of age or physical or mental disability. Factors (11) and (17) did not apply. Factor (14) applied in one defendant's case as the offense was committed while on a form of release for a felony conviction. The enhancement factors warranted increasing defendants' sentences to ten years. Defendants' fines were reduced to $50. The trial court erred in concluding under Tenn. R. Evid. 609 that a defendant could be questioned on cross-examination about his prior guilty plea; however, the error was harmless.


OUTCOME: The judgments were affirmed; the fines imposed were modified to $50 each.

State v. Martin

2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 739

September 18, 2007, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Sevier County. No. 10470-II. Richard R. Vance, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Sevier County (Tennessee), which convicted him of reckless homicide in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-215. He received a four-year sentence to be served on probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by a jury of one count of reckless homicide, a Class D felony, and received a four-year sentence to be served on probation. Defendant was the general manager of an amusement park and the State attempted to prove that defendant attached a jumper wire to the electrical panel of a ride in order to bypass its safety restrictions. A passenger fell to her death on that ride after her harness opened. The appellate court affirmed the conviction, stating that the evidence was sufficient. If the jury accredited the testimony of various witnesses, including amusement park employees, it could have rejected defendant's theory that the jumper wires were on the ride before it arrived at the amusement park, and accepted the State's theory that defendant had placed the wires on the ride. Additionally, the presence of the jumper wire on the ride created a substantial and unjustifiable risk of injury or death to those who rode it. Judicial diversion was not appropriate because defendant's exemplary lifestyle did not outweigh the circumstances of the offense, the need for deterrence, and the interests of the public.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Dellinger v. State


No. E2005-01485-CCA-R3-PD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 682


December 19, 2006, Session 
August 28, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected August 28, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Dellinger v. State, 2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 832 (Tenn. Crim. App., Oct. 12, 2007)
Appeal granted by Dellinger v. State, 2008 Tenn. LEXIS 111 (Tenn., Feb. 25, 2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at Dellinger v. State, 279 S.W.3d 282, 2009 Tenn. LEXIS 252 (Tenn., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Blount County. No. C-14432. D. Kelly Thomas, Jr., Judge.
State v. Dellinger, 79 S.W.3d 458, 2002 Tenn. LEXIS 207 (Tenn., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was convicted in the Circuit Court for Blount County (Tennessee) of first degree murder and sentenced to death. After his request for postconviction relief was denied, petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner argued, inter alia, that counsel was ineffective for failing to offer proof through another expert after the defense was unexpectedly confronted with the testimony of a rebuttal expert near the end of petitioner's proof. The court of appeals disagreed. Counsel testified that during a break, they discussed this development but decided not to move for a continuance. Counsel said that the issue of the victim's time of death was "hotly contested" and that the defense had already put on their expert proof through the testimony of their expert, which they considered damaging to the State's case. Counsel said that the defense had conferred with a forensic pathologist, but determined not to call him on petitioner's behalf because his opinions did not support their defense. Petitioner failed to demonstrate that counsel provided ineffective assistance. Counsel said that after being presented with the testimony, they conferred and decided not to seek a continuance. The decision was partly the result of lack of awareness of any measures the defense could have taken to counter the testimony. Under the facts presented, the decision not to challenge the testimony was not unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

581 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Coburn


No. E2005-02730-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 623


December 19, 2006, Session 
August 9, 2007, Filed


NOTICE: ORDERED NOT FOR CITATION. PLEASE CONSULT THE TENNESSEE SUPREME COURT RULES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Ordered Not for Citation October 6, 2008.
Appeal denied by State v. Coburn, 2008 Tenn. LEXIS 764 (Tenn., Oct. 6, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Sullivan County. No. S46,918-19. R. Jerry Beck, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal Court for Sullivan County (Tennessee) of aggravated kidnapping and attempted rape. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that his convictions for both aggravated kidnapping and attempted rape violated due process. The court of appeals agreed. The entire attack lasted only "ten to twenty-five" seconds and consisted of only a brief struggle between the victim and defendant. While upon first consideration it might have appeared that defendant had a sexual purpose based upon the fact that he attacked the victim in the nude and in a state of "semi-arousal," the victim's testimony focused on being pulled and pushed "constantly" toward the foliage around the trail. Because the victim fought off defendant, he was scarcely able to remove the victim from the path and was able to restrain her for only thirty seconds or less. Even though defendant might have ultimately acted in a manner that evidenced an intent to commit a rape and a distinct kidnapping, it could not be concluded from the facts that he did more than that which was necessary to attempt to subdue the victim in order to commit rape. Defendant did not clearly evidence a separate purpose and intent to kidnap the victim. Therefore, the struggle and resulting detention was "essentially incidental" to the attempt to rape.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for aggravated kidnapping was dismissed. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

 

582 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Fly


No. E2006-01979-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 599


March 28, 2007, Session 
July 26, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgments of the Criminal Court are Reversed and Dismissed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Greene County. No. 06CR018. James Edward Beckner, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court are Reversed and Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty in the Criminal Court for Greene County (Tennessee) to possession of cocaine with intent to sell or deliver while employing a deadly weapon and unlawful possession of a weapon. Defendant appealed via certified questions of law.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress evidence because the officer had already issued the citations to defendant and the time frame for "running the dog around" the vehicle without any suspicion or cause had expired. The court of appeals agreed. The dog was trained to detect the presence of drugs, not items such as bolt-cutters or stolen lawn mowers. Moreover, the officer's initial concerns about defendant's being intoxicated were quickly dispelled following the officer's face-to-face encounter with defendant. No facts developed after the officer's approach of defendant's vehicle that independently supported conducting a canine sweep of the vehicle. The officer testified that defendant became "nervous" when the officer asked him for consent to search the vehicle; however, the court of appeals rejected that observation as a sole, independent basis for conducting the dog's sweep. There was no justification for delaying the detention for the purposes of using the drug dog, even if it was done "real quickly." When the officer gave defendant the citations, the legitimacy of the detention ended.


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated and the case was dismissed.

 

583 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Goods v. Parker


No. W2006-00849-CCA-R3-CO


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 589



July 24, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Goods v. Parker, 2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 600 (Tenn. Crim. App., July 24, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Lake County. No. 03-CR-8494-R1. R. Lee Moore, Judge.
Goods v. Parker, 2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 893 (Tenn. Crim. App., Oct. 13, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Lake County (Tennessee), which granted a petition for habeas corpus relief filed by petitioner inmate.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was released to his mother after he was charged with theft of a vehicle. Shortly thereafter, he committed several other felonies. Defendant later entered a global plea agreement to many charges. The inmate then filed a petition for habeas corpus relief, which alleged that the sentences were illegal because they should have been consecutive. The trial court granted relief, and this appeal followed by the State. In affirming, the appellate court determined that it was not bound by the State's stipulation that the inmate was out on bail when the second crimes were committed because this involved a legal interpretation of Tenn. R. Crim. P. 32(c)(3). Next, the appellate court rejected the State's argument that the inmate's claim was not yet ripe because the inmate was alleging that all of the sentences were illegal. Finally, the appellate court held that the inmate was out on bail within the meaning of Rule 32(c)(3) when the second crimes were committed. A recognizance bond was a bail security. There was no difference between those released on a promise or a money bond. Because the law required consecutive sentences in this case, the concurrent sentences imposed were illegal.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed. The case was remanded to a criminal court for further proceedings.

 

584 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Davis


No. M2006-00198-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 580


January 23, 2007, Session 
July 19, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by State v. Davis, 266 S.W.3d 896, 2008 Tenn. LEXIS 776 (Tenn., 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 2003-D-2992. Seth Norman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) of first degree premeditated murder, assault, and attempted second degree murder. Defendant was sentenced to, inter alia, life imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his convictions of first degree premeditated murder and attempted second degree murder. The court of appeals disagreed. Two witnesses testified that defendant approached the victim on the sidewalk and slapped her across the face after engaging in an angry verbal confrontation. Defendant threatened to shoot at the victim's residence and warned her not to be there when he came back. One witness said that he was standing outside the victim's apartment and could see the victim standing in front of the living room window. The witnesses both observed defendant return to the apartment a few minutes after the confrontation on the sidewalk. Defendant pulled out a gun and shot into the open living room window, then sprayed the front of the apartment with bullets from right to left. After the shooting, defendant left the crime scene and drove off in his car. All of the shell casings in front of the apartment were fired from the same gun. There was no evidence that anyone inside the apartment was armed at the time of the shooting. Therefore, the evidence was sufficient to sustain defendant's convictions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

585 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Banks


No. W2005-02213-CCA-R3-DD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 536


April 10, 2007, Session  
July 6, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected July 26, 2007.
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Corrected by State v. Devin Banks, 2008 Tenn. LEXIS 963 (Tenn., Nov. 7, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 03-01956. Joseph B. Dailey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) of first degree premeditated murder, criminal attempt to commit first degree murder, and especially aggravated robbery. Defendant was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his first degree premeditated murder conviction. The court of appeals disagreed. There were numerous circumstances from which the jury could have concluded that the murder was premeditated. For example: (1) the victim was unarmed; (2) the particular cruelty of the killing, as evidenced by defendant ordering the victim to lie face down and, in execution style, shooting the helpless victim in the head; (3) defendant securing a weapon prior to the murder; and (4) calmness immediately after the killing as shown by defendant leaving the crime scene and proceeding to go on a shopping spree. Defendant's argument that he lacked the requisite mental state for premeditated murder was not persuasive. Defendant's own statement confirmed that the execution-style murder of the victim was committed without passion and was completed after defendant had removed valuables from the home. A jury could have found the essential elements of premeditation and intent beyond a reasonable doubt. Thus, defendant did not meet his burden of proving that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction for premeditated murder.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Tankesly v. State

OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred by failing to instruct the jury on aggravated sexual battery and attempted aggravated sexual battery as lesser-included offenses of child rape. The appellate court found that defendant waived the issue under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-106(g). He found crack cocaine and marijuana in the car's steering wheel. The trial court acted properly in granting defendant's motion to suppress the fruits of an unlawful search. The officer's search of defendant's vehicle was not authorized by the search warrant.

Haynie v. Bell


No. M2006-02752-CCA-R3-CV


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 486


April 18, 2007, Session  
June 22, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 06C-786. Thomas W. Brothers, Judge.
Haynie v. State, 2002 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1139 (Tenn. Crim. App., Mar. 26, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, denied petitioner inmate's petition for a writ of habeas corpus. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate, serving a sentence of nine years for two convictions for passing worthless checks, alleged that his judgments of conviction were void. The inmate argued that the affidavit in support of the arrest warrant was insufficient. The appellate court found that this argument was without warrant as all questions as to the sufficiency of a warrant were foreclosed by the finding of an indictment. The indictment referenced the statute defining the offense; as such, the indictments against the inmate were valid. The victim, by accepting partial payment, did not make an election of remedies pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 47-29-101 as there was no notice to the victim that the accounts were closed at the time either check was passed by the inmate to the victim. A determination of whether the inmate was entitled to relief based on an alleged violation of Brady would require an evidentiary hearing, and this was precisely why habeas corpus relief was not appropriate.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 458



June 11, 2007, Filed

Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Stay denied by, As moot Mobley v. Tenn., 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 169689 (E.D. Tenn., Oct. 13, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed As Modified. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Knox County. No. 78699. Ray L. Jenkins, Judge.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal Court for Knox County (Tennessee) of two counts of first degree murder, especially aggravated robbery, and setting fire to personal property. The trial court sentenced defendant to two consecutive life sentences plus twenty-two years. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his convictions for first-degree murder. The court of appeals disagreed. Defendant called one victim to set up a meeting because defendant owed the victim money for crack cocaine. Defendant took his gun with him, got into the car with the two victims, and shot them both. Defendant pushed the driver out of the car and drove off with one of the victims still in the passenger seat. There was testimony that defendant appeared to be changing the music as he drove away from the crime scene, and he nodded to a witness as he drove by. Defendant pushed or dragged one victim down a hill behind a church in an attempt to hide his body. Defendant had his stepmother check into a motel where he disposed of money and drugs, and smoked a marijuana cigarette. When defendant attempted to leave the motel room, he was arrested. Additionally, there was testimony that defendant acted as if nothing was wrong in phone conversations shortly after the killings. All of that evidence fell under the factors that a rational jury could have used to infer premeditation on the part of defendant.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentences for his convictions for especially aggravated robbery and setting fire to personal property were modified from twenty to eighteen years and from two years to one year, respectively. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

State v. Hannah


No. E2005-02833-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 441


February 20, 2007, Assigned on Briefs  
June 6, 2007, Filed

Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Hannah, 2008 Tenn. LEXIS 417 (Tenn., June 23, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Hamilton County. Nos. 254484, 254485, 254486, & 254487. Rebecca J. Stern, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a judgment of the Criminal Court for Hamilton County (Tennessee) granting defendants' motion to suppress evidence that was seized as a result of the search of their car following an unconstitutional stop.


OVERVIEW: An officer stopped defendants' vehicle after observing it traveling below the posted speed limit. Defendants were subsequently charged with possession of cocaine. On appeal of the trial court's decision granting defendants' motion to suppress, the court affirmed, holding that the officer did not have a reasonable suspicion to believe that defendants had committed a crime or were about to commit a crime when he initiated the traffic stop. The proof showed only that the officer observed defendants' vehicle traveling within the bounds of the speed limit while other vehicles traveled 10 miles per hour in excess of the speed limit. There was no minimum speed limit posted on the road. The officer testified that traffic was able to pass defendants' vehicle in the right hand lane rather than being forced to stop by defendants' reduced speed, and therefore defendants were not violating Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-18-154(a).


OUTCOME: The judgment granting defendant's motion to suppress was affirmed.

State v. Eggleston


No. M2006-00210-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 429


October 25, 2006, Assigned on Briefs  
May 30, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Eggleston, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 852 (Tenn., Sept. 24, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Circuit Court are Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Marshall County. No. 16292. Donald Harris, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Marshall County (Tennessee) of five counts of child rape and four counts of aggravated sexual battery. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress statements to police because he requested an attorney and because the officers failed to advise him of his Miranda rights. The court of appeals disagreed. Detectives testified that the door to the school office was not locked, and another detective testified that she did not tell defendant that he could not leave the office. After the interview, the detectives did not arrest defendant, and he returned to class. Defendant was not in custody during the interview. In any event, a detective testified that she Mirandized defendant before the interview, that defendant signed a waiver of rights form, that he gave a statement, that he signed the statement, and that he never requested his attorney. The record reflected that defendant signed a waiver of rights form and that he initialed each of his rights. Defendant testified at the hearing that he understood his rights and gave a statement. Defendant was advised of his Miranda rights and voluntarily gave a statement. Therefore, the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Siliski


No. M2004-02303-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


238 S.W.3d 338; 2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 390


December 12, 2006, Session  
May 15, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Siliski, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 878 (Tenn., Sept. 17, 2007)
Related proceeding at Byrd & Assocs., PLC v. Siliski, 2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 561 (Tenn. Ct. App., Aug. 19, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Circuit Court Affirmed and Remanded for Resentencing. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Williamson County. No. II-CR03192. R. E. Lee Davies, Judge.
State v. Siliski, 2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 747 (Tenn. Crim. App., Sept. 27, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Circuit Court Affirmed and Remanded for Resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Williamson County (Tennessee), which convicted her of nine counts of animal cruelty in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-14-202(a) (2003). She was sentenced to concurrent terms of 11 months, 29 days at 75 percent for each conviction, all suspended except for 10 days, with the remainder of time to be served on supervised probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of 11 counts of animal cruelty and the trial court merged the convictions involving the same animals, resulting in 9 convictions. Defendant was sentenced to concurrent terms, all suspended except for 10 days, with the remainder of the time to be served on supervised probation, followed by unsupervised probation. The appellate court affirmed the convictions, but concluded that the trial court erred by ordering consecutive periods of probation in conjunction with concurrent sentences. Accordingly, the appellate court remanded for resentencing. Under the plain language of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-14-202(a), a person committed "an offense" who tortured or maims "an animal" or failed unreasonably to provide necessary food, water, care, or shelter to "an animal" in his or her custody. The use of the plural in the separate penalty provision in § 39-14-202(d) did not create any ambiguity in the definition of the offense in § 39-14-202(a), which clearly provided that a single animal could form the basis for an offense. Additionally, the statute was not unconstitutionally vague as applied.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the convictions but remanded for resentencing.

Sweatt v. State


No. M2006-00289-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 381


February 13, 2007, Assigned on Briefs  
May 9, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Sweatt v. State, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 836 (Tenn., Sept. 24, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 90-S-1362. Steve Dozier, Judge.
Sweatt v. State, 2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 832 (Tenn. Crim. App., Sept. 30, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate pleaded guilty in the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) to two counts of aggravated rape. After the inmate's second petition for postconviction DNA testing was denied, the inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued that the trial court erred by denying his second petition for DNA testing. The court of appeals disagreed. The inmate himself admitted that DNA analysis had previously been conducted on both himself and the victim in June 1990. However, he argued that he did not receive the results, which he claimed unequivocally excluded him as the perpetrator, prior to his guilty plea. The court of appeals, in affirming the dismissal of the inmate's prior petition for DNA analysis, found that not only were the results given to the inmate six months prior to entry of his pleas, they also were "inconclusive." Thus, the inmate was not excluded as the perpetrator. Moreover, the inmate made no allegation that any new type of forensic analysis could resolve issues not resolved by the previous analysis. As noted by the State, the law of the case doctrine was applicable because a separate panel of the court of appeals had previously found that the inmate failed to meet the criteria in Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-304 for DNA analysis, specifically "that the evidence was never previously subjected to DNA analysis." Thus, review revealed that summary dismissal of the petition was proper.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Bowles v. State


No. M2006-01685-CCA-R3-HC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 355


April 17, 2007, Assigned on Briefs  
May 1, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 96-C-1534. Mark J. Fishburn, Judge.
Bowles v. Bell, 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 49358 (M.D. Tenn., Aug. 4, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed the judgment of the Criminal Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, denying his petition for habeas corpus relief.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted in 1997 of especially aggravated burglary, aggravated rape, robbery, aggravated burglary, and attempted rape. He was sentenced to serve his fifty-year sentence at one-hundred percent. In the habeas court, he alleged that his trial counsel rendered deficient performance, and that he suffered a procedural default which would entitle him to federal habeas corpus relief. He also alleged his sentence was in violation of Blakely. Because petitioner's Blakely claim would merely make his conviction voidable, not void, he was not entitled to relief. Blakely was not to be applied retroactively to cases. Further, petitioner's ineffective assistance of counsel claim was not cognizable in a habeas proceeding in Tennessee, because it required the introduction of evidence from outside the record. Petitioner had already brought the claim in a post-conviction petition, and the cause and prejudice standard did not require the state habeas court to consider a procedurally defaulted claim.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the habeas court was affirmed.

State v. Thompson


No. E2005-01790-CCA-R3-DD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 328


July 26, 2006, Session  
April 25, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by State v. Thompson, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 657 (Tenn., Aug. 13, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed as Modified. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for McMinn County. Nos. 89-705, -06, -07. Jon Kerry Blackwood, Judge.
State v. Thompson, 151 S.W.3d 434, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 995 (Tenn., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed as Modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for McMinn County (Tennessee), which had convicted him of first-degree murder in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-202(a)(1) (1989) and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction, stating that he failed to meet his burden of establishing that he was incompetent to stand trial either before or during his trial. Additionally, defendant did not successfully invoke his right to represent himself at trial. Thus, his right to self-representation was not denied. With the exception that defendant made no effort to conceal his crime, there was evidence of all of the indicators of a deliberate, premeditated killing. And, a reasonable-doubt instruction did not impermissibly raise the degree of doubt required for acquittal or correspondingly decrease the State's burden of proof in violation of defendant's due-process rights. Although it would have been more complete to advise the jury that premeditation required the exercise of reflection and judgment under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-201(b)(2) (1989), the instruction, as given, did not incorrectly define premeditation or mislead the jury. Defendant's sentence was modified to a sentence of life imprisonment based on a balancing and proportionality review.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction for first-degree murder but modified his sentence of death to reflect a sentence of life imprisonment.

 

596 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Daniel


No. M2006-01620-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 315


April 18, 2007, Assigned on Briefs  
April 20, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Daniel, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 698 (Tenn., Aug. 13, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 98-B-922. Cheryl A. Blackburn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) sentenced defendant after his probation was revoked due to an arrest for driving under the influence. Defendant challenged the sentence and the constitutionality of Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-36-106(e)(3)(B), which prohibited credit from being given for time spent on probation.


OVERVIEW: The trial court did not abuse its discretion in revoking defendant's probation because it rightfully considered the drunk driving arrest in determining whether he had violated the terms of his probation. The exclusionary rule would not have barred consideration of the arrest, even if the stop that led to the arrest were found to have been unconstitutional in the collateral proceeding, as there was no evidence of police harassment. Defendant was not entitled to relief on his claim that Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-36-106(e)(3)(B) was unconstitutional as there was a distinction between community corrections and probation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

597 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hugghis


No. W2006-01149-CCA-R3-CO


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 282



April 3, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Hugghis, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 675 (Tenn., Aug. 13, 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Hugghis v. Tenn., 2008 U.S. LEXIS 1459 (U.S., Feb. 19, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3; Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. Direct Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 94-02837-47. Chris Craft, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed Pursuant to Rule 20, Rules of the Court of Criminal Appeals. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant petitioner, who appeared pro se, sought post-conviction relief. The trial court treated the motion as one for habeas corpus relief. The petitioner appealed from the dismissal of the petition. The State filed a motion requesting that the decision of the Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) be affirmed, pursuant to Tenn. Ct. Crim. App. R 20.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner entered guilty pleas to five counts of aggravated burglary, one count of attempt to commit first degree murder, four counts of aggravated rape and one count of aggravated sexual battery. In the instant proceeding, the petitioner challenged the statutes under which he remained convicted. Specifically, he challenged the validity of the statutes, asserting that they failed to contain an enacting clause as required by the Tennessee Constitution. The trial court pointed out that the original Tennessee Public Acts enacting the laws under which defendant was convicted were all properly signed by the Speakers of the House and Senate of Tennessee, and signed by the governor of Tennessee. They were then within a year codified into the Tennessee Code with proper authentication. The trial court had proper jurisdiction over defendant's person, and the laws under which the defendant was prosecuted were validly enacted. The appellate court verified that the original legislation was properly enacted. Moreover, the matter satisfied the criteria of Tenn. R. Ct. Crim. App. 20.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

598 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Turner


No. M2005-02749-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 256


October 25, 2006, Assigned on Briefs  
March 16, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Turner, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 608 (Tenn., June 25, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court is Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Marion County. No. 7139. Thomas W. Graham, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court is Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Circuit Court for Marion County (Tennessee) found defendant guilty of misdemeanor assault. After a sentencing hearing, the trial court sentenced defendant to 11 months and 29 days to be served at 75 percent. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant tried to sell the victim and his friends a pornographic DVD. The victim asked defendant if he was a child molester. Defendant got upset and shook a bat at the victim and his friends. They left. Two days later defendant saw the victim and hit him on the head with a baseball bat. The trial court asked the jury to continue deliberating, did not direct its comments to jurors in the minority, and did not urge jurors to acquiesce to the views of the majority. While the better practice would have been for the trial court not to make any comment regarding a possible retrial of the case, the trial court did not mention anything about the time, effort, or expense of a retrial. Thus, the trial court did not give the jury an improper instruction. In addition, despite the incorrect facts in the presentence report and the trial court's misstatement of the facts, the trial court properly sentenced defendant because (1) he had a prior conviction for second degree murder; (2) he had no hesitation about committing a crime when the risk to human life was high; and (3) the victim's statement to defendant two days before the assault did not justify his being hit on the head with a bat.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

599 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Webb


No. E2006-00736-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 200


December 19, 2006, Session  
March 5, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Reversed in Part; Remanded. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Hamilton County. No. 256728. Don W. Poole, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Reversed in Part; Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty in the Criminal Court for Hamilton County (Tennessee) to bribery of a public servant. The trial court imposed a ten-year sentence as a Range III, persistent offender. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court of appeals initially found that the trial court improperly classified and sentenced the defendant as a Range III, persistent offender. There was no means of determining if defendant's convictions under the Georgia statute were based on actions that would have resulted in convictions under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-17-504. Defendant also argued that his sentence violated the constitutional prohibition against cruel and unusual punishment. The court of appeals disagreed. Considering defendant's prior criminal convictions and his unsuccessful attempts at rehabilitation, the sentence was not grossly disproportionate to his offense and did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment. It was clear from the transcript of the guilty plea hearing that defendant was aware of the sentencing range for bribery of a public servant, a Class C felony--three to fifteen years depending on his range classification. Moreover, the imposition of consecutive sentencing was authorized by Tenn. R. Crim. P. 32. Finally, any revocation of defendant's probation in Georgia resulting from the conduct giving rise to the present charges was simply a consequence of defendant's continued criminal activity.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded to the trial court for resentencing. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

 

600 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Goods v. Parker


No. W2006-00849-CCA-R3-CO


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 190


October 3, 2006, Session  
February 27, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Tenn. R. App. P. 3 Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Lake County. No. 03-CR-8494-R1. R. Lee Moore, Judge.
Goods v. Parker, 2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 893 (Tenn. Crim. App., Oct. 13, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Lake County (Tennessee), which granted appellee inmate's petition for habeas corpus relief.


OVERVIEW: The inmate, while a juvenile, was brought into juvenile court upon a petition alleging delinquency for theft of a vehicle. He was released to his mother after a detention hearing. Just a few months later, he was back in juvenile court on charges of especially aggravated robbery, second degree murder, and attempted second degree murder. Thereafter, a global plea agreement was entered. In a subsequent habeas corpus proceeding, the parties stipulated that the inmate was out on bail when he committed the second batch of crimes. The trial court found that the inmate's sentences were void because consecutive sentences were mandated under Tenn. R. Crim. P. 32(c)(3). The State's motion for reconsideration was denied, and this appeal followed. In reversing, the appellate court determined that the stipulation was impermissible under Tennessee law because it was interpreting the meaning of a court rule. Next, the claim was ripe because the legality of all the sentences was raised. Finally, the appellee court found that a juvenile could not have been released on bail since he could not have been arrested, pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-11-105, 37-1-113.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court was reversed, and the habeas corpus petition was dismissed.
